Current Affairs Commentary

Where Will Industry and Commerce Draw Funds? 21

— Lun

Shares in Chinese companies have never had a public market or a mechanism for circulation. When they have appeared, they have been as fleeting as the epiphyllum, ultimately ending up with a listed price but no actual market. As a result, it is difficult for buyers to buy and difficult for sellers to sell. This is one reason why investment in companies is not enthusiastic and why company development is not easy. Examining the reasons for this, it is true that the general public lacks a deep understanding of company businesses. However, after decades of industrial development, how many Chinese enterprises have achieved remarkable success? Even those hailed as major industrialists often suffer from poor management. An examination of their internal operations reveals them to be disorganized, chaotic, and unstructured, their emptiness beyond description. As for those who, through a stroke of good fortune, achieve temporary prosperity but fail to sustain it and ultimately fail, the instances are even more numerous. To try to inspire public confidence in investing in companies under these circumstances is like traveling south by heading north. On the other hand, some companies are well-managed. If one wishes to purchase their shares, they are often unattainable even at a price higher than that offered by stockbrokers. Conversely, there are no buyers if one wishes to sell. This is because, if shares have a public market, their market price often changes rapidly depending on the company's business situation. Before a company's business is on track, changes in the share market can easily lead to unforeseen disadvantages for the company. The fact that company shares are not publicly traded is also due to unavoidable circumstances.

The situation for company shares is already like this. Let us now consider company bonds. The raising of company funds is motivated by two reasons. One is to develop new businesses. Increasing capital is feared to increase permanent burdens, so bonds must be issued to meet temporary funding needs. The other is a lack of funds. Adding shares is difficult, so issuing bonds is the only option. Regardless of how the company bonds are used, they are ultimately secured by the company's assets for principal and interest. If the public has deep trust in its assets, then increasing capital by adding shares is easy, and issuing bonds is also easy. Without this trust, bonds cannot be raised. Although some company bond issues are completed in no time, their position is different. Their operations have their own advantages, enabling them to gain public trust.

Since the financial industry experienced an accident, depositors have been deeply anxious. Hoarding cash is unprofitable, and there are no channels for investment. As a result, the adventurous tend towards speculation, while the prudent, mindful of the timely payment of principal and interest on various bonds in recent years, use their savings to purchase bonds. As a result, various industries are depressed, while only the securities market flourishes. Although bond prices sometimes weaken, they are bound to rise again. This is because they maintain their creditworthiness and gain public trust. Moreover, the security for bonds is customs duties, which are generally considered the most reliable form of security. If the security for the principal and interest of various bonds were not customs duties but marketable securities such as shares, and of various types, it would be difficult to gain the same level of public trust.

Observing various figures, the lack of silver reserves is a fact. However, if no effort is made to remedy this, it will not only remain lacking but will eventually be depleted. From another perspective, Chinese idle capital is suffering from a lack of safe havens. Much of it even flows into foreign banks and hides overseas. If this idle capital could be used in industry and commerce and kept within domestic banks, it would greatly benefit industry and commerce. However, how can we prevent it from fleeing and make it available for our use? This depends on the efforts of those who wish to utilize it. The way to do this is not difficult. The key is to abandon selfish secrecy and make the content of the business public in order to gain public trust. However, if companies cannot reveal their true situation to the world, then finding self-generated rescue plans will inevitably rely on thorough investigation and careful auditing. This is what is meant by seeking the next best option out of necessity. It is said that in the world of commercial warfare, deception is unavoidable. But it is not known that doing business is not comparable to conducting military operations. In military operations, deception is used, making the empty appear full and the full appear empty, showing people the unpredictable. However, in industry and commerce, except for technical aspects where secrecy should sometimes be strictly maintained, matters that can be made public in business should be revealed truthfully so that the public has room for assessment. Over time, their credibility will become firm. I believe that the greatest reform today is to abandon self-interest and do one's best within oneself, being strict with oneself and lenient with others. Then there may be hope for a turnaround in business.

Methods for Mediating the Italian-Abyssinian Dispute: Italy Expresses Acceptance, Not Exceeding Mussolini's Demands, Several Points of the Draft Resolution Still Need Modification, No Problem for the League of Nations to Pass It 22

(Geneva) The Council of the League of Nations is currently working to find a solution to the Italian-Abyssinian dispute, and its own fate is almost tied to this effort. Late yesterday, Eden (England), Laval (France), and Aloisi (Italy) broke the deadlock and agreed on a draft resolution, which was immediately telegraphed to Italian Prime Minister Mussolini. His approval or disapproval will be decided by Mussolini this morning. (Reuters, 4th)

(Geneva) The draft resolution to resolve the Italian-Abyssinian dispute, agreed upon last night by British cabinet member Eden, French Premier Laval, and Italian representative Aloisi, has now been accepted by Italy. Therefore, the proposal is certain to pass at the League of Nations Council meeting. Prime Minister Mussolini's reply telegram regarding the compromise draft arrived here today, with slight modifications, but they will not cause difficulties. Therefore, the reply is tantamount to acceptance. It is believed that if there are no objections to the mediation process, the modifications requested by Mussolini all relate to subsequent steps. After studying Mussolini's reply telegram with experts today, Italian representative Aloisi and French Premier Laval immediately sent the original text to British representative Eden and Abyssinian representative Haile Selassie. (Reuters, 2nd)

(Geneva) The League of Nations this morning postponed its intervention in the Italian-Abyssinian dispute until mid-September. The United Kingdom, France, and Italy have agreed on a compromise plan, which is generally seen as a victory for Italy. This plan restores the work of the League of Nations arbitration committee within the scope of Mussolini's demands. Once Italy agrees tomorrow, the League of Nations will notify Abyssinia of this plan. If Abyssinia can accept it sooner, the Council may be able to formally pass it on Friday evening. According to this plan, French Prime Minister Laval, British representative Eden, and Italian representative Aloisi reached an agreement after repeated meetings within 24 hours. During the secret meetings, the three tried to avoid any measures opposed by Mussolini, and as a result, they agreed on two compromise methods: first, regarding the scope of the arbitration negotiations; second, regarding the fundamental procedures for resolving the Italian-Abyssinian dispute. (National Telegram, 1st)

(Geneva) Yesterday, when the three statesmen considered the French draft containing Eden's amendments, there was a significant divergence of opinions between Britain and Italy. Britain refused to accept the two opposing suggestions made by Italy regarding the draft: one concerning the provision that Italy should not resort to force during the negotiations, and the other concerning Abyssinia's participation in the negotiations of the signatory countries to the 1906 treaty, namely Britain, France, and Italy. Britain insisted on Eden's amendments. Later, Eden, Laval, and Aloisi worked hard to communicate their opinions. The main difficulty at that time was Italy's insistence that the League of Nations Council should not be involved in the negotiations between Britain, France, and Italy. The three representatives finally agreed on a compromise: deleting the mutually contested clauses regarding the League of Nations' involvement in the three-country negotiations, and leaving this matter to be decided separately by the three countries. The three countries will formally declare their readiness to negotiate with the relevant fourth party in the spirit of the 1906 treaty. This method satisfies Britain in substance and Italy in form. However, everything now depends entirely on Mussolini's decision. (Reuters, 2nd)

British, French, and Italian Representatives Agree on Draft Resolution: Contains Four Points 23

(Geneva) British Minister Without Portfolio Eden, French Premier and Foreign Minister Laval, and Italian representative Aloisi held talks at the French delegation office from 7:15 PM to 8:20 PM. The contents of the draft resolution of the League of Nations Council were discussed and agreed upon. Then, experts jointly drafted the text of the resolution. (Havas, 1st)

(Geneva) After the representatives of the United Kingdom, France, and Italy agreed on the draft resolution of the League of Nations Council, Italian representative Aloisi consulted Italian Prime Minister Mussolini by telephone. At 4:00 PM, Aloisi informed French Premier and Foreign Minister Laval of Mussolini's opinion. Laval then held talks with Eden. As a result, the Council meeting originally scheduled for 5:00 PM this afternoon was postponed to tomorrow. It is reported that the measures in the draft resolution agreed upon by the representatives of the United Kingdom, France, and Italy are divided into the following items: (1) The Council appoints a fifth neutral arbitrator to agree with the arbitrators of Italy and Abyssinia to establish a reconciliation method before September 1, in accordance with the procedures stipulated in the 1928 Italian-Abyssinian arbitration treaty. (2) The Council acknowledges that the Walwal border issue is not within the jurisdiction of the arbitration committee. (3) The United Kingdom, France, and Italy, which signed the 1906 treaty on Abyssinia, should immediately begin negotiations to seek a solution that guarantees good relations between Italy and Abyssinia with the Abyssinian government. (4) The League of Nations Council should reconvene on September 4, and reports should be submitted by all parties concerned. It is said that Italy has generally accepted the above points. In addition, the United Kingdom advocates that the resolution should stipulate that Italy and Abyssinia agree not to resort to force during the negotiations. Mussolini is not opposed to this point, but believes that the existing treaties are sufficient to guarantee that armed conflict will not occur after the failure of negotiations. Therefore, the resolution only states that Italy and Abyssinia agree to abide by the provisions of existing treaties in the event of a breakdown in negotiations. The biggest difficulty in the current negotiations lies in the issue of the League of Nations' mission. Britain and France both advocate that the three signatory countries to the 1906 treaty should negotiate a way to resolve the Italian-Abyssinian dispute within the framework of the League of Nations, while Italy opposes any form of intervention by the League of Nations. No agreement has yet been reached on this matter. Although Laval has made every effort to mediate, Italian representative Aloisi has recently informed Laval that Mussolini will not reply tonight. (Havas, 1st)

(Geneva) The key points of the reconciliation plan created by the representatives of the United Kingdom, France, and Italy after a long negotiation last night have been revealed to the world through discussions between League of Nations representatives and journalists this morning. This place is now quietly waiting for Italy's reply, and it is expected that there will be no more changes. This is because the compromise reached by Aloisi with Eden and Laval is not inconsistent with the instructions he received from Mussolini. The compromise plan is to entrust the fifth arbitration committee to continue its work, but only to examine the Walwal incident and not to discuss border issues. The arbitration work must be completed before the end of September. As for other matters, the United Kingdom, France, and Italy should discuss solutions through diplomatic channels based on the 1906 Three-Power Treaty. If Italy can accept this plan, the three-country meeting will be held in Italy next week. The location is approximately Vatican Termiglia. The reservation regarding the League of Nations Council's intervention in the entire Italian-Abyssinian issue has been abandoned. However, Italy must sign a gentleman's agreement with the United Kingdom and France, preparing to discuss the Abyssinian issue at the next Council meeting. Whether Abyssinia will be invited has not yet been decided. Once Italy's formal reply is received, the full text of the resolution to be proposed in the League of Nations will be formally notified to the Abyssinian authorities. (National Telegram, 2nd)

Abyssinia Remains Calm Awaiting League of Nations Resolution; People of All Genders Share the Same Hatred of the Enemy 25

Addis Ababa: The official circles here are very calm on the surface regarding the progress of the Geneva negotiations, but it is noteworthy that they believe the League of Nations trusteeship proposal is aimed at dealing with Italy. The Abyssinian government firmly believes that this plan will not be approved by Italy, because Italy hopes to monopolize East Africa. Thousands of troops passed through the capital yesterday and set off northward, but they were not allowed to enter the city, in order to avoid the attention of reporters and the diplomatic community. The government is now doing its best to promote self-defense among the people. Two group exercises were held yesterday. The first was convened by the Patriotic Youth League, and its mission was to instill the principles of colonial warfare in the rural people. The second was convened by Abyssinian women. Some women even carried weapons. At the women's meeting, speeches were given to encourage women to live and die with men. However, these speeches were not of a nature that fostered hatred of foreigners. A total of 83,000 yuan was donated at the two meetings. At the same time, the government is preparing for the capital's air defenses to avoid air raids. The entire city is divided into two parts, and some foreigners have voluntarily taken on the task of training Addis Ababa police. (National Telegram, 2nd)

It has been found that these rivers originate in Abyssinia and flow into Somalia. Addis Ababa, Abyssinia: "Voice of Abyssinia," the only daily newspaper here, which is popular and printed in "Amharic" (the name of a central region of Abyssinia), recently published an article, saying, "If Abyssinia's policy is wavering, it will increase Italy's intention to invade. We want peace, but we can only achieve it by adopting an unyielding attitude. In short, if Italy advocates peace, we are prepared to listen to it. On the other hand, if it is belligerent and warlike, we will not hesitate to deal with it." Currently, the Abyssinian people are waiting for the resolution of the League of Nations Council with a calm attitude. Speeches are given daily in 40 churches in the capital and its suburbs. (London) During today's meeting in the Lower House, the opposition party initiated a debate on foreign affairs. British Parliament Adjourns for Summer; Unemployment Continues to Decline; Trade Shows Significant Improvement 33

(London) Although the international situation is rather bleak, the British Parliament adjourned today in high spirits for the summer. The number of unemployed people in the country has now continued to decline, and the business situation has also improved, especially in the steel industry. The trade statistics for the first six months of this year are particularly encouraging. The banknotes circulating in British banks are often an indicator of public prosperity and credit reliability. According to the bank's report, the total number circulating this week is 19,000,000 pounds more than in the same week last year. The number of unemployed last month, according to informal sources, was 1,970,000. According to a report from Middlesbrough, it increased by more than 30% compared to June. The increase in refined steel was even greater, reaching 26,647 tons, an increase of 10,000 tons compared to the previous month. This is due to the demand in many parts of the world, especially in South Africa, Finland, India, China, and Argentina. At the same time, many manufacturers are now engaged in manufacturing cold-rolled steel sheets for the motor industry. This product was previously a specialty of the United States. The Southern Railway and the Northeastern Railway are now planning to extend their lines and electrify the railways, which will cost millions of pounds. At the same time, there are many people in the UK on vacation. Travel by rail, ship, and plane has broken previous records. The railway companies are now planning to add 1,000 trains at the end of the week for vacationers to use by the sea. The number of sleeping car berths ordered from Ostend has reached 4,000, and the number of train seats has reached 13,000. American and Russian Aviators Prepare for Arctic Flight, Post Departs San Francisco for Russia, Seeking a Shortcut to Connect European and American Skies 38

(San Francisco) The famous American long-distance aviator Post, accompanied by his wife, departed by plane today, planning to cross the top of the world to reach Moscow. This one-eyed aviator is now making a non-stop flight to Seattle. However, floats are installed under the plane to cross the Bering Sea. After arriving in Moscow, Mr. and Mrs. Post will go to the swimming island and Greenland and then return to the United States. The purpose of this trip is to measure the sky routes between Alaska and Siberia for commercial airlines, seeking a shortcut to connect Europe and America. Post is currently flying a new-style Lockheed low-wing single-engine aircraft. (1st Reuters dispatch)

(Moscow) The famous Soviet Russian aviator, Captain Levonevsky, recently plans to fly through the Arctic to reach the United States. Professor Shmidt, Director of the Northern Shipping Administration, recently spoke on this plan, saying, "If this flight plan can be completed, then based on the reports obtained along the way, and with detailed research, it will not be difficult to establish a regular airmail route between Russia and the United States via the Arctic. As for preparing for this flight, the most important thing is climate reports along the way. Good weather is a necessary condition for flying over the Arctic. The weight of the aircraft to be used this time will be reduced to the lowest possible level, but its total weight will still reach eleven tons, because the aircraft carries 7,200 liters of gasoline and 500 liters of engine oil, which weighs six tons. Therefore, the aircraft must fly low when taking off to be effective. The most worrying danger along the way is the problem of icing on the outside of the wings. At present, there is no equipment to avoid this danger. In addition, the crew carries enough food for three months, so that if the aircraft is forced to land in the Arctic, the crew will not be cut off from food. In addition, an icebreaker will take care of it near the Arctic to prevent emergencies. The aircraft used this time is the same as the aircraft that created the round-the-world flight record in 1934. This record is 11,000 kilometers, but in theory, it can fly 30,000 kilometers." According to reports, the departure date of the aircraft has not yet been determined and will depend on the weather. It may depart this afternoon or at night. It is not yet certain whether foreign reporters will be able to visit the airfield at that time. (1st Havas dispatch)

The Communist International Congress Passes Important Resolutions, Urging Abandonment of Sectarian Disputes 40

(Moscow) The Seventh Congress of the Communist International passed a resolution yesterday recommending that communist parties in various countries abandon sectarian disputes and form a united front with other parties against imperialism, capitalism, and fascism within their respective countries. The resolution also stipulates that communist parties in various countries should maintain their autonomy and have freedom of action in internal affairs. As for the cadres of the Communist International, they only retain the guiding authority on general theory and serve as a liaison between communist parties in various countries. According to reports, this resolution is the first resolution of the Seventh Congress, and the Congress is still continuing. (2nd Havas dispatch)

Hindenburg's Death Anniversary, All of Germany Flies Flags at Half-Mast to Express Mourning, Tannenberg Commemorates the Deceased Hero 41

(Berlin) It has been a year since the death of the late German President Hindenburg last year. Today, people across Germany held a one-year commemoration to show their respect and gratitude. Although people across the country were not ordered to suspend business, flags were flown at half-mast everywhere to express mourning. Leader Hitler also expressed his admiration for Mr. Xing. Tannenberg, where Hindenburg defeated the Russian army during the Great War, has now become a place for German patriots to commemorate. Although the sky was dark, countless people came to Hindenburg's tomb to lay wreaths, especially women. The largest of the wreaths was presented by Hitler. (2nd National Electric dispatch)

The Number of Souls Killed Under Automobile Wheels in New York Exceeds the Number of American Military Casualties in the European War 42

(New York) The police department, in view of the heavy traffic in New York City and the alarming number of vehicle accidents each year, has posted notices widely in the thoroughfares to awaken pedestrians and pay attention to traffic safety. The notices compared the number of war casualties with the number of traffic accident casualties in the city, saying, "During the European War, the American troops sent to Europe fought for eighteen months, with a total of 50,310 killed in action and 182,674 wounded. As of May 20 of this year, statistics show that 51,200 people died in the United States due to vehicle accidents in eighteen months, and 1,304,000 were injured. It can be seen that the damage is even greater than that of war." (1st Havas dispatch)

Interpretation of "The New Criminal Law Does Not Punish Conduct" 49

(Nanjing) The Ministry of Justice has decided on the following interpretation of the ambiguities in the new criminal law that does not punish conduct: Although the new criminal law does not have articles such as accomplice, their conduct should still be discussed separately according to the circumstances as the crime of instigation or assistance, and it is not exempted from punishment. Therefore, cases in which the original determined judgment cited the articles of accomplice and sentenced, should still be executed according to the judgment. Also, although Article 230 of the new criminal law, incest, is limited to direct relatives or collateral relatives within three degrees of kinship, if it is incest among relatives, attention should still be paid to the provisions of Article 228 of the new criminal law. The provisions of Article 228, Paragraph 3 of the new criminal law are only a reason for exemption from punishment, and their conduct should still be considered a crime (2nd Central News Agency Electric dispatch)

Ambiguities Arising After the Repeal of the Ordinance for Punishing Bandits 53

(Nanjing) The Judicial Yuan explained the ambiguities arising after the repeal of the Ordinance for Punishing Bandits as follows: (1) Those who have not yet been transferred to the provincial government should be handled in accordance with the usual procedures of criminal prosecution; (2) Those approved by the provincial government before July 1 have been determined by the original judgment, and should still be executed according to the judgment, except in cases of re-appeal and extraordinary appeal; (3) For those whose original judgment has not yet been determined, they should be allowed to appeal according to the usual procedures. As for the appeal deadline, if the judgment has been served, it should be filed from July 1, and if it has not been served, it should be served again, and filed from the date of service. (2nd Central News Agency Electric dispatch)

Reasons Why the Income Tax Has Not Been Implemented 54

(Nanjing) The income tax was originally scheduled to be levied on July 1, but it is said that the reason for the failure to implement it on schedule is that party members have already paid income donations, and the income tax stipulates that civil servants (regardless of party affiliation) must pay taxes in accordance with the law. The Central Party Headquarters believes that there are a large number of party members who are civil servants. Paying income donations and then paying income tax is an increase in the burden on party members, and the names are similar, which is not conducive to public opinion. The Central Committee is studying in detail how to abolish income donations without affecting party fee income, so that the income tax can be implemented as soon as possible. (2nd Special dispatch)

Severe Flooding in Tianmen, Hubei Province 79

Over 80,000 People and Livestock Drowned - Countless Public and Private Losses

A correspondent in Hankou reports that the flood in Hubei Province was most severe in Tianmen and Hanchuan. The disaster in Tianmen was particularly dire due to its low-lying terrain and intricate network of rivers. The people relied on the dikes for their lives. On July 7th, the Xiang River surged violently, and the 11-bow section of the Xiang River main dike in Zhongxiang County collapsed. The flood rushed directly into the county, rising more than 19 feet overnight, exceeding the highest historical water level by more than 5 feet. On the morning of the 8th, Commissioner and County Magistrate Shi Yuling went to Yuekou to supervise the people in rescuing the Yuekou dike section, which fortunately remained safe. However, the Shuanghe Dyke, 15 miles downstream of Yuekou, ultimately collapsed late at night amidst wind and rain, extending to 72 embankments, all of which were breached. The 72 embankments, surrounding over a hundred miles, encompassing areas of Tianmen, Mianyang, and Jingling counties, were all submerged. At the same time, the county river's water level continued to rise. The commissioner's office and all its staff, along with the security team and local organizations, desperately tried to rescue the city walls, increasing their height and thickness, hoping to preserve the county town. Unexpectedly, by 8:00 AM on the 9th, the water level became increasingly fierce, and the city walls immediately overflowed and collapsed, flooding the city higher than the crenellations. When the dike collapsed, more than a dozen security team soldiers and civilians who were rescuing the dike were washed away, and the rest had nowhere to go. When the flood entered the city, the West Gate bore the brunt of the impact. Some 300 families had their people, houses, and belongings washed away, some had their houses washed away but some people survived, and some had their houses remaining but their people were annihilated. In an instant, the entire city was submerged. Except for the north and south city towers and the top of the ancient city dike outside the North Gate, all institutions, schools, blockhouses, and barracks were either completely destroyed or severely damaged. Seven or eight tenths of the city walls collapsed. The roofs of the commissioner's office could be navigated by boat. In the rural areas, the eighth district was the worst affected. Hundreds of towns and villages, such as Huiputou City, were completely destroyed, and livestock, grain, clothing, and other items were washed away. Subsequent investigations revealed the following losses: (1) The disaster area covered approximately 6,300 square miles, accounting for seven-eighths of the county's area. (2) The affected population was approximately 124,000 households, totaling 643,000 people, accounting for eight-tenths of the county's population. (3) The flooded farmland accounted for 1.4 million mu out of the county's total of 1.79 million mu, representing eight-tenths of the total. (4) Over 16,000 houses collapsed, and approximately 40,000 houses were submerged but not yet evacuated. (5) The number of deaths due to drowning was highest in the first, eighth, fifth, and twenty-fourth districts, with approximately 12,000 people. (6) Over 28,000 head of cattle, 32,000 pigs, and 5,500 horses were drowned. (7) Approximately 350,000 dan of washed-away grains, beans, and wheat. (8) 130,000 dan of unharvested cotton, over 700,000 shi of soybeans, and over 800,000 shi of rice. (9) Public losses included over 300 miles of telephone lines erected over the years, running vertically and horizontally, and over 500 miles of county and district roads built over the years. In this flood, the telegraph poles, wires, bridges, and roadbeds were all washed away completely. Other public buildings, such as the commissioner's office, Confucian temple, various institutions, school buildings, and newly built blockhouses, and repaired city walls, were also destroyed. When news of the county's disaster arrived, it was said that no less than 100,000 people had drowned. According to a detailed investigation, 80,000 people have been rescued, but the water has not yet receded, and the disaster victims have nowhere to shelter, facing hunger and disease. If relief is delayed, they will ultimately perish. (August 1st)

The Summer Season Gradually Passes: Business Declines in Guling 80

--Vacant Houses for Rent Are Everywhere--

A correspondent from Guling reports that Mount Lu is vast and majestic, with tranquil scenery, embracing rivers and lakes, and convenient transportation. The mountain rises over 4,000 feet above sea level, and the summer temperature is often around 80 degrees Fahrenheit, making it a popular summer resort for Chinese and foreigners. Mount Lu spans over 500 li, with Guling as its center. The usual resident population is only three to four thousand, but it increases to forty to fifty thousand during the summer. Especially after 1930, important central figures often came to discuss national affairs, and dignitaries gathered, adding to its prosperity. Last year, the demand for houses in the mountains exceeded supply, and hotels and shops were making several times their usual profits. For example, the Lujinfang, Jiaotong, Qingliang, and Yuntian hotels earned profits exceeding ten thousand for the most successful, and at least several thousand for the less so. However, with the summer season almost over this year, vacant houses for rent are still everywhere, the streets are deserted, and business is less than three-tenths of what it was last year. The reasons are: (1) The cost of living on Mount Lu is very high. For those staying in hotels, a minimum living expense of two yuan per person per day is unavoidable. Those who travel around the mountains by sedan chair need at least eight yuan a day. In this period of economic decline, there are very few who can afford such extravagance. (2) The Yangtze River area has been severely flooded, and business is in decline. The compradors from Yichang, Shashi, and Hankou, who used to come to the mountains to escape the heat, are also fewer in number this year. (3) Many of those who used to come from Nanjing, Shanghai, and the lower reaches of the Yangtze River to escape the heat have switched to Qingdao and Beidaihe. For these reasons, the business of Mount Lu, including major stores and hotels, has been greatly affected. (July 29th)

Page 11

Cahar Authorities Rescue Two Foreign Journalists 81

German Journalist Returns Safely to Beiping - Details Encounter with Bandits

A Beiping correspondent reports that the British journalist Jones and the German journalist Miller (also translated as Mi and Bai), who were kidnapped by bandits in Baochang County, eastern Chahar Province, have been rescued due to the strenuous efforts of the Chahar provincial authorities. The German journalist Miller escaped from the bandit den on the 30th of last month. After briefly staying in Baochang and Zhangjiakou, he arrived safely in Beiping this (1st) morning at 7:10 AM, escorted by Zhai Weiqi, an official dispatched by the Chahar Provincial Government. Everyone was delighted by Miller's safe return. The Military Affairs Committee sent Councilor Yang Quanzhong and Special Diplomatic Commissioner Cheng Xigeng to Miller's residence to express their condolences. Miller expressed his infinite gratitude for the enthusiasm of our government authorities in rescuing him. This (1st) noon, he went to the British and German embassies to report on his encounter with the bandits at the same time as the British journalist Jones and his personal escape, and to discuss ways to rescue Jones. He is scheduled to travel to Zhangjiakou tomorrow (2nd). A reporter visited Miller at 3:00 PM this (1st) afternoon, and he recounted his experience of encountering the bandits. The details of his account are recorded as follows:

At the Time of the Encounter with Bandits

I (Miller referring to himself) and Mr. Jones departed from Duolun at 10:00 AM on the 27th of last month by automobile to Zhangjiakou. After passing through Huangqidaying and Habaka, the car suddenly malfunctioned in a desert area. We spent the night there. The next morning, after the car was repaired, we continued our journey. At noon, we arrived at Hejiadahuofang Village in Guanmagou. Before the car reached the village, a group of about thirty or forty bandits wearing blue uniforms (similar to the uniforms of the security team) suddenly rushed out from both sides and fired dozens of shots from rifles and machine guns. Two bullets hit the water tank of our car, forcing us to stop.

Confiscation of Property

I (Miller referring to himself) jumped out of the car and asked them why they were shooting and stopping us from moving forward. The bandits replied, "We are the bandit suppression security team." They then invited me into a small house for tea. At that time, I caught a glimpse of the bandits carrying my luggage into the house. I asked them why, and they claimed it was a routine inspection. One of the bandits then put my money into his pocket. I angrily asked if taking people's property was also part of the inspection. The bandit laughed and said, "We are bandits, not the security team. Since you have come, please settle in." The bandits then dragged the British journalist Mr. Jones from the car into another small house and hung him from the beam with a rope. After a while, they brought him back to my room, seemingly to negotiate.

Four Demands

At that time, the room was surrounded by bandits standing guard, holding guns in a ready-to-fire position. The situation was extremely serious. Under these circumstances, the bandits made the following four demands: (1) a ransom of 100,000 yuan; (2) 40 rifles and 20,000 rounds of ammunition; (3) 20 pistols and 20,000 rounds of ammunition; (4) 20 portable machine guns and 20,000 rounds of ammunition. Without discussion, they immediately wrote these four demands on a piece of paper and asked us to sign it, giving us ten days to fulfill them, otherwise they would tear up the ticket. The note was handed to the Russian driver Peter Lixuefu and my servant Liang, who departed from Guanmagou at 3:00 PM and went directly to Baochang County. After the driver and others arrived at their destination, they used the telephone to report to a relative of the driver named Qi in Zhangjiakou, who relayed it to the British Embassy and the German Legation in Beiping. The county magistrate of Baochang also telegraphed the provincial government to report the kidnapping.

Life in the Bandit Den

Until the evening of the 29th, after the British and German embassies received the phone call from Zhangjiakou, they dispatched personnel on the morning of the 30th to leave Beiping at 6:00 AM and arrive in Zhangjiakou at 2:00 PM to handle the rescue. While we were trapped in the bandit den, we were treated well, so we did not suffer significant mental trauma. However, Jones was frightened because it was his first encounter, while I found it to be the most interesting event of my life, as life in the bandit den had its own unique charm. After the driver and Liang left Guanmagou and headed south on the 28th, Jones and I, under the coercion of the bandits, with our hands tied behind our backs, rode horses north, moving from place to place. It can be seen that the bandits were not familiar with the geography, as they circled left and right but still did not leave the territory of Baochang County. On the 29th, we finally moved to Yemqi. Although we were moved around haphazardly, fortunately, we were not lacking in food and drink.

Rescue Situation

On that day, Zhang Yunjie, a platoon leader of the security team, along with three policemen, came to negotiate. The bandits first fired at Zhang, who indicated that he was unarmed with a white towel. The bandits sent someone to talk to Zhang. Zhang took out a letter from the team headquarters as proof of his identity. Unexpectedly, the bandit leader was illiterate and tore the letter into pieces. He then tied up Zhang and the other three people and brought them to the bandit leader. The bandit leader, whose surname was Ji or Ji (not confirmed), first asked them to release us. The bandit leader, seeing Zhang's bravery and skill, voluntarily offered to concede, reducing the ransom to 50,000 yuan and waiving all other demands.

Escape Experience

On the 30th, after eating together in Kethier, the bandits separated us. My group consisted of six riders (including security team platoon leader Zhang Yunjie and three policemen, two of whom were guides). I initially thought the odds were against us, or that I was going to be shot, but unexpectedly, I arrived safely in Baochang County. Zhang's negotiations with the bandits resulted in my parole so that I could negotiate the ransom with various parties. The bandit leader also said that if the government would allow them to turn over a new leaf, they would be willing to accept amnesty. I arrived in Baochang at noon on the 30th. At 4:00 PM on the 31st, I returned to Zhangjiakou by car and met with Xiao Zhenying, the person in charge of the Chahar Provincial Government, and Miller, the military attache sent by the British Embassy, to discuss ways to rescue Mr. Jones. Mr. Xiao expressed his agreement and promised to use all means of tactful compromise to ensure Jones's safe return.

Jones' Safety

Regarding the safety of Mr. Jones, if effective rescue measures can be taken before the deadline, there should be no cause for concern. According to unofficial news, Jones has already escaped. After inquiring with various parties, this has not been confirmed. However, I hope that the rumors are true and offer my sincere prayers. Assuming that Jones is still in the bandit den, I plan to go to Zhangjiakou tomorrow (2nd) to assist in the rescue of my friend in need. If there is still no solution, then I will go to Baochang and return to the bandit den to share life and death with Jones, to fulfill my moral obligation. The Chinese government has provided sincere assistance to us in this incident, and I have boundless admiration. (August 1st)

Guangdong Province: Second Major Flood in the Dong River 82

Heyuan and Zhaoqing Experience a Sudden Rise of Over Ten Feet - Huilai Experiences Flash Floods, Destroying All Fields

A Guangzhou correspondent reports that Guangdong Province's West River recently suffered a major flood, and the disaster situation in counties such as Guangning, Sihui, Gaoming, and Gaoyao was extremely severe. The counties are currently handling local disaster relief. In addition to the government allocating 1,000 yuan to each county and the Renai Charitable Hall distributing over 10,000 jin of rice, the Renai Charitable Hall recently resolved to allocate 40,000 yuan in relief funds to assist the disaster victims in Guangning and Sihui counties. However, just as the West River's situation was improving, the East River flooded again. The East River had already experienced a major flood before the West River disaster, causing significant losses along the river. It was thought that after the East River had receded, the West River would flood, and the East River would be spared a second flood. Unexpectedly, misfortunes never come singly. Starting on July 21st, the East River experienced continuous strong winds and heavy rain, and the river level suddenly rose by over ten feet, causing flooding along the East River basin again. In Heyuan County, the city was flooded starting on the 25th. In the city's Taiping Road and Hualong Bridge areas, the water was over five feet deep on the ground. Residents' furniture was floating everywhere, and countless livestock were drowned. The embankments of Laolong Town in Longchuan were also submerged. The roadbed of the Guanghe section of the second provincial highway in the eastern district was submerged, and the Waxi Bridge on the Zijing-Wuhua section of the third highway (from Huizhou to Xingning) was destroyed. Traffic was suspended on the 25th. Downstream, in counties such as Huiyang and Boluo, the river level also rose at the same time. In Huiyang, the water level rose by more than nine feet in areas such as Sandu, Pingshan, Pingtan, and Xinxu. Below Pingshan, areas such as Mahuang Temple, Niuxu, Shanchang Street, Shaibu Chang in Huicheng, Xiamei Street, and Tangxia were all knee-deep in water. Boluo, located downstream, anticipated a second flood due to the upstream flooding. Currently, farmers are rushing to harvest the rice day and night, fearing that the flood will submerge everything, leaving no grain left. Therefore, crowds gather in the fields day and night to harvest, creating a chaotic scene. In Huilai County, located northeast of Huiyang, torrential rains have continued for the past ten days, causing flash floods this month. The water in the county's fourth district is over ten feet deep, sweeping away all the rice and crops, resulting in an unprecedented disaster. The fourth district chief and others have submitted a request to the county government for relief, stating in the petition: "A petition is submitted to request relief to comfort the disaster victims. The area under my jurisdiction is low-lying, and the Longxi River runs through the middle. The river is shallow and narrow, with sand and gravel accumulating, causing frequent floods and droughts. The agricultural villages have already fallen into bankruptcy. Selling sons and daughters is a common occurrence. However, Heaven has not been kind and has brought down another calamity. Starting on the 6th of this month, heavy rains have poured down without stopping day or night, causing flash floods. The water on the ground is over ten feet deep, turning all the fields into a watery land. All the rice crops, which were bearing fruit and about to ripen, were suddenly submerged and completely destroyed for six days and nights. At this time of devastation in the villages, another major flood has occurred. Early rice crops have been lost, and the means of livelihood have been cut off. Rice prices have soared in recent days, and wails of anguish can be heard everywhere. The voices of people crying for food are unbearable to hear. I, as a representative of the people's will, am heartbroken by what I have witnessed. The disaster situation is so severe that I cannot bear to keep it from your attention. Therefore, I respectfully submit this document detailing the disaster situation for your examination and approval. I humbly request that you forward this to the higher authorities to seek relief and comfort the disaster victims. Upon submission, I am at a loss for words to express my heartfelt entreaty." (July 27th)

Qingdao Municipal Government Strictly Prevents Silver Export 84

—Provisional Measures for Exchanging Silver Dollars—

A Qingdao correspondent reports that the Qingdao Municipal Government has formulated five provisional measures for citizens to exchange silver dollars in order to prevent the export of silver and maintain the city's financial stability. These measures are intended to restrict the exchange of silver and prevent unscrupulous individuals from secretly transporting it out of the city. A notice has been issued to all government agencies and the public to inform them of these measures. The notice and the measures for exchanging silver dollars are listed below:

Municipal Government Notice

It has been found that our country uses silver as its main currency. Sufficient silver reserves ensure convenient circulation and a sound economy. However, since the price of silver has increased, exporting silver has become highly profitable. Therefore, incidents of exchanging banknotes for silver dollars and secretly transporting them out of various places have been occurring from time to time. This government has repeatedly received clear orders from the central government to prohibit such activities and has issued orders to strictly investigate and ban them. In the past, merchants, both Chinese and foreign, in this city have been able to consider the overall situation, and there have been few such incidents. However, recently, the number of silver dollars exchanged by banks daily has gradually increased, indicating that there are unscrupulous individuals attempting to transport them out of the city secretly. If this outflow is allowed to continue unchecked, it will not only affect the financial stability of this city and hinder trade between Chinese and foreign merchants, causing harm to both Chinese and foreign merchants, but it will also lead to the collapse of the national economy, endangering the foundation of the country. Therefore, it is necessary to strictly prevent this from happening and eliminate this hidden danger. The following five provisional measures for banks and money shops in Qingdao to exchange silver dollars are hereby formulated and will be implemented from the date of promulgation in order to maintain the market. In addition to issuing this notice by this government and sending it to the Municipal Chamber of Commerce, it is hereby copied and sent to you for your information. This order is issued.

Measures for Exchange

(1) In Qingdao City, these measures are formulated to alleviate the impact of silver outflow on financial stability. (2) When people exchange banknotes at banks, the banks should first provide yuan notes for circulation. If there is a need to use silver dollars, they may provide a limited amount of silver dollars, but the number should not exceed ten yuan per person. (3) If merchants need to exchange a large amount of silver dollars for legitimate purposes, they should declare the purpose. After the Chamber of Commerce verifies and approves it, the government will notify the bank to exchange the silver dollars accordingly. (4) These measures must be implemented by all Chinese and foreign merchants in this city. The Municipal Government will notify the Municipal Chamber of Commerce and the Banking and Money Shop Guilds to inform their members to comply with the measures. It will also ask the consuls of various countries stationed in Qingdao to notify their merchants to comply. (5) These measures will be implemented from the date of promulgation of this notice by the Municipal Government.

Songjiang: Township Head Retains Queue, Ordered to Cut It Off

This county has received orders to organize township heads, gather them in Songjiang, and provide them with knowledge of the baojia system. All districts have been able to strictly comply with the orders and diligently implement them. However, Feng Luyuan, the head of the fourth bao of the Puhua Township in the sixth district of Peinan, secretly asked someone to replace him after reporting for duty. This was discovered by the county government, which immediately summoned the township head for reprimand. It was also found that the township head was still wearing a queue coiled inside his hat. He was severely reprimanded and ordered to have his queue cut off in the court by the police.

A Glimpse of Summer Hygiene Work 85

The County Public Security Bureau, regarding public health in the urban and rural areas and road cleaning as particularly important during this summer season, followed provincial orders to organize a hygiene committee. The bureau chief, district chief, and head of the hygiene section serve as ex officio members, and local figures Cai Zhongyu, Zhu Jiuwang, and Du Gui were hired as members. The committee has been established. In addition to the original street cleaners from the district office continuing to serve, the committee hired ten additional street cleaners to work together. A portion of their work includes removing melon rinds and filth from city rivers, banning open-air latrines, and donating funds to purchase and prepare "ke fa sha" (heatstroke relief) medicine. They entrusted the First District Office to distribute four bottles per "jia" (a neighborhood unit) to the "jia" head's office, for the needs of each household within the "jia." Currently, the committee's work is quite active.

Wuxi: Appealing to the Ministry of Finance to Implement Currency Reform

The local guilds of wine and soy sauce shops, tobacco retailers, the tobacco industry, restaurants, and other related businesses, noting the prevalence of copper coins in the county market and the soaring price of silver dollars (each dollar can be exchanged for approximately 3,600 cash coins, a difference of over 800 cash coins compared to the previous rate of 2,800 cash coins per dollar), submitted a petition. The guilds, consisting of small-capital shops, pay for goods in silver dollars but receive cash coins for sales. Given the current economic decline in rural areas and the sluggish business conditions, they find it difficult to raise prices, resulting in significant losses. If no relief measures are taken, a collapse is feared. Recently, the Ministry of Finance specially organized a currency system research committee, which decided to adopt a decimal system with ten "jiao" (dimes) equaling one yuan (dollar) and ten "fen" (cents) equaling one "jiao." It was also decided to mint new subsidiary coins made of nickel and antimony in denominations of 5 li, 1 fen, 2 fen, 1 jiao, and 2 jiao. The central mint would produce these coins, and the Central Bank would distribute them to various banks to circulate in the market and support commerce and industry. In this time of commercial crisis, this would be like timely rain after a long drought. The guilds jointly submitted a petition to the Ministry of Finance yesterday, requesting prompt implementation to provide relief and alleviate the distress in Suzhou.

Changzhou: Public Security Bureau Police Affairs Meeting

The Wuyi Public Security Bureau convened a county-wide police affairs meeting on the afternoon of the 1st. Attendees included the heads of various sections within the bureau, as well as the heads of various sub-bureaus, inspectors, and others. The meeting was chaired by Bureau Chief Xu Baoguang. The following resolutions were passed regarding important cases: (1) Registration of domestic dogs and methods for capturing and killing rabid, sick, and stray dogs. It was resolved that rabid and sick dogs should be immediately captured, killed, and buried to prevent harm. The bureau will draft methods for dealing with domestic and stray dogs and submit them to the county and then to the provincial office for review and implementation. (3) Concerning the dangerous practice of riding bicycles on the streets without sufficient skill, it was resolved that bicycle shops would be prohibited from renting bicycles to unskilled riders. All rented bicycles must have lights at night, and violators will be punished. Beat police will be responsible for strict enforcement at all times. (4) It was decided to convene a training session for the secretaries of all sub-bureaus and stations at the bureau on the 6th of this month. (5) It was resolved to strictly prohibit the performance of local operas and gambling in rural teahouses in various townships. Other cases were briefly mentioned.

Nantong: Intensifying Landslide Along the Langshan Riverbank

The landslide along the Nantong riverbank has recently intensified. The Yao Dong riverbank has retreated, having been breached by a large tide for over 300 "zhang" (approximately 1,000 meters), creating a critical situation. People along the river have been conscripted to protect the riverbank day and night. Currently, Langshan Mountain is getting closer to the river. When the high flood season arrives, it will immediately enter the river. Local funds for bank protection are insufficient. The County Construction Committee plans to divert 30,000 yuan from funds raised to rebuild the ancestral hall of the national hero Cao Ding for bank protection purposes. A stone bank will be built and named Cao Gong Dike. At the same time, a telegram will be sent to the provincial and central authorities for subsidies for the project. The Hangzhou city government's riverfront bathing area at Zhakou, covering over ten "mu" (approximately 0.67 hectares), is conveniently located along the car road. The bathing area is surrounded by bamboo fences and small pavilions and has two flat buildings serving as men's and women's changing rooms and toilets. It has been completed. The opening ceremony was held yesterday (the 1st) at 4:00 PM. Over a thousand people attended, including guests from various organizations, swimming enthusiasts Xu Shaodi and Huang Huabiao, the Changfeng Swimming Team, the Boy Scout Summer Camp, and students from the police academy. Mayor Zhou Xiangxian reported on the preparatory process, which cost a total of 2,400 yuan. The performances then began. Over twenty members of the Changfeng team participated, with their formation being orderly and resembling swimming dragons. Thirty members of the Zhejiang Provincial Boy Scout cadre, led by Liuhe Pagoda, arrived and performed water polo and swimming techniques.

Letter: Letter from Zhou Xuewen and Others 88

To the esteemed chief editor of Shen Bao:

We are writing in response to Tang Zhigao's letter of July 27, which was a response to the court's examination of the stolen corpse bones case. His letter, titled "Correction," actually confuses the public. Therefore, we must clearly expose the truth to uphold justice. The Nijiatan (mud altar) is a local public property, with ownership belonging to the local public. In 1915, Songjiang County Magistrate Li Ji and the official in charge of land reclamation, Di, jointly issued a proclamation permanently prohibiting encroachment. No one is allowed to privately hope to take possession of it. This is because the land is where Li Zhigang of the late Ming Dynasty buried his writing tablet, and it has long been respected by local people. However, Tang Zhigao claims that the ownership of the land belongs to the "Jiazi Disaster Memorial Association" and identifies himself as a representative of the memorial association. From this, it is clear that Tang Zhigao and others have long intended to encroach on the altar. The demolition and excavation this time were deliberate actions planned in advance. It should be known that the two title deeds for the altar, referring to the 7 fen and 8.6 li owned by the Yin family and the 6 mu, 1 fen, and 4.8 li owned by the Zhang Shude family (as mentioned in the original letter), include the deed for the Zhang Shude family, which was donated back to the local citizens by Zheng Bocang and others, and was not redeemed by the Memorial Association. How can it be falsely claimed to be owned by the Memorial Association? In 1932, when Zhang Jiecai attempted to seize the altar, a meeting was held at the County Chamber of Commerce, and a public resolution was made to investigate and resist the original plan. At that time, Gu Shisheng was still a representative of Zhang Jiecai and stood against Tang Zhigao. Tang Zhigao ran around appealing to everyone, and presented the deed, saying it would be permanently preserved. Now, the Yin family deed has surfaced, and it turns out that Tang Zhigao and Gu Shisheng have colluded. They have been planning to encroach on and utilize the altar ever since. The Disaster Memorial Association is just a facade. However, the Disaster Memorial Association is a temporary memorial meeting for people affected by war, not a permanent legal institution. Tang Zhigao is the representative of the meeting, also only a temporary representative chosen at the meeting, not a lifetime representative. Then the Disaster Memorial Association itself is like a spark of fire or a flash of lightning, only appearing for a moment. How can Tang Zhigao and others use the name of the association to implement means to seize the Nijiatan? Moreover, both times the Nijiatan was registered, the first time in 1915 by Jiang Shilun and many others, and the second time in 1926 by Yao Jun and ten others, were all local citizens and did not use the name of the Disaster Memorial Association. And Tang Zhigao was also one of those listed in the document. Looking back, it's as clear as yesterday, how can he have forgotten? These are obvious facts, and the public land is officially documented. Tang Zhigao still dares to fabricate and deceive. If he can falsely claim this, what can't he falsely claim? Since the Nijiatan is a public property that is permanently prohibited from encroachment and is not the private property of the Jiazi Disaster Memorial Association, then Tang Zhigao, Yin Shisheng, and two or three other private individuals cannot use the name of the Memorial Association to dispose of the altar. This is very clear. With this in mind, it can be seen that the so-called meeting of directors and supervisors held at the County Chamber of Commerce on September 21, 1934, as mentioned in the original letter, was an infringing act by a few private individuals like Tang Zhigao and cannot reduce their responsibility for encroaching on, destroying, and excavating the altar. Moreover, since the altar had been registered as permanently prohibited from encroachment, anyone who wanted to do anything with it would have to submit it to the competent authorities for approval. Otherwise, it would be a private action, and especially since the event was an intentional encroachment, the act violates the current criminal law. As for the excavated corpses, 31 wooden boxes have been collected, and it was publicly agreed to seal them and choose a date for a joint burial. Why, without waiting for the date, did they hire workers to bury them privately at night? This time, when the prosecutor came to the scene to excavate and inspect, why did the location not match what was indicated? Why were there fewer boxes? Why were some seals there and some not? Why were the bones in the boxes dry and wet? And why was there an empty box? Why doesn't Tang Zhigao explain these doubts one by one to clear up public suspicion? Also, the original letter stated that all expenses, except for the 621 yuan contributed by the Pastor Bu, were raised by the association's colleagues. It is unknown that Pastor Bu's 621 yuan was his celebration money, which Pastor Bu intended to donate to the orphanage as an educational fund. Tang Zhigao violated his wishes and asked someone to find a way to get it to be used for demolishing the pavilion and destroying the tomb. Pastor Bu still feels pained when he talks about it. As for the other expenses, since the soil was sold for money to cover the costs, and the altar could be used to generate income in the future, who wouldn't be happy to temporarily pay for it to gain endless benefits in the future? But they changed the name to fundraising. This is truly what is called "eloquent lies." Furthermore, the original letter said that since the memorial pavilion was planned to be built on the land in 1925, no coffin has ever been buried there, and the burial of wounded soldiers in 1927 is even more of a substitution. According to the information, there were as many as 48 wounded soldiers buried in 1927, and the wounded soldier roster of the Fifth Sanatorium clearly states the date of death, burial date, and location, and it was also reported to the Chinese Red Cross Society headquarters, with records available. Furthermore, the leader of the burial team, Yu Zhanjing, can be questioned. How can they call a deer a horse, and replace things to cover the public's eyes and ears? When the National Revolutionary Army fled from Hangzhou in 1927, Sun Chuanfang retreated to Songjiang. The army of Wu gathered in Songjiang, and when the Zhili-Lu army was redeployed, Bi Shucheng's 37th Brigade, He Dianjia's 39th Brigade, and Deng Xishan all stationed at the station and the infant nursery, while the military police inspection office was stationed at the fire brigade. Therefore, the wounded soldiers buried by the Fifth Sanatorium after the National Revolutionary Army recaptured Songjiang, it happened at this time. Tang Zhigao has not heard of it, and he hastily referred to the transplantation, referring to a shelter as a horse, which is really a muddled head, eye holes like a bean-like view. The above reasons are all facts seen by everyone and consistent public opinion, not personal opinions. We are afraid that the original letter is called a correction, and if it is not revealed, it will be enough to confuse right and wrong. We have stated the facts in detail and ask you to include them in the letter column for public viewing, so that the truth may be known. This is our letter.

Respectfully,

Zhou Xuewen, Chairman of the Songjiang Branch of the Chinese Red Cross Society, Li Xiuzhe, President of the Sijing Branch, and Huang Xiaohe, a citizen of Songjiang.

Local News

Fish Industry Holds Regular Meeting Yesterday: Credit Loans to be Paid by Qian Zhuang (Money Shop) 89

The Shanghai Fish Industry Association held its 22nd regular meeting of member representatives of the second term at its office on Ningbo Road at 2:00 PM yesterday. Representatives Pei Yunqing, Shao Yanshan, Liu Wuqiao, Wang Huailian, Chen Shengwu, and over fifty others from 55 companies, including Dade, Dalai, Yuansheng, Wufeng, Renchang, Shengchang, Ankang, Anyu, Cunde, Tongrun, Tongyu, Renchang, Jintai, Hengxun, Yida, Henglai, Huifeng, Shunkang, Yisheng, Yichang, Fuyuan, Fukang, Futai, Shenyuan, Gengyu, Jukang, Hengjiu, Hengtong, Baofeng, Hongsheng, Hongfeng, Hongxiang, Dingkang, and others, attended. Chairman Qin Runqing reported on (1) the minutes of the previous meeting, (2) incoming and outgoing documents for July (36 incoming, 528 outgoing), and (3) the 24 meetings held by the industry at the association in July. He also gave various reports on the preparation of the warehouse. Matters for discussion: 1. Please decide on the July discount interest rate. Resolved: 6.95%. 2. In the past, the Jiangsu Provincial Department of Finance used Water Conservancy Construction Bonds to borrow 500,000 yuan from the association. The general assembly resolved that the association would temporarily pay 50,000 yuan per month from the preparation warehouse until it was fully paid, and then the member shops would allocate the costs evenly to repay the preparation warehouse. Now, 450,000 yuan has been paid by the preparation warehouse, and the Water Conservancy Bonds have been received. Should the payment and collateral be allocated to each shop? Please discuss and decide. Resolved: To be evenly distributed among the shops. 3. The case of 5,000,000 yuan in small industrial and commercial credit loans. The association resolved to undertake 250,000 yuan to be evenly shared by the member shops. Now that the small loans have begun to be issued, how should the funds recognized by the association be raised? Please discuss and decide. Resolved: To be temporarily paid by the Qianye Joint Reserve Bank. The meeting adjourned around 3:00 PM.
