— (Bai Ding)

Although it is said that "every profession produces its own expert," people are actually "complaining about every profession they are in." This is truly an inexplicable philosophy.

People in society admire the happiness of school life, but when they recall their student days, how much they wanted to enter society! However, in the end, society disappoints them.

Goethe said, "No girl is bad at being sentimental, and no boy is bad at falling in love." The concept of love between men and women is that men are dewdrops, while women are just hidden.

"Okay, you wait and see, I'll show you what's what later." It is said that this is the last trump card of our Ah San. However, what is "what's what"? That remains unknown.

A friend who was complaining about the literacy campaign said, "Damn it, literacy? Does literacy mean we won't even have food to eat?" Alas! This is the good nature of the citizens of the Republic of China.

Stupid people are called "honest"; bad people are called "smart."

Private School 149

— Zhu Weixuan

I accidentally passed by ×× Lane and suddenly heard a chaotic sound of reading, which aroused my curiosity. Without hesitation, I stepped into the gate of No. × and temporarily acted as an uninvited guest.

It was a small room with extremely poor lighting. Inside, there were four or five dirty square tables, each filled with children who had sallow complexions and were malnourished. Some were hunched over writing, some were reading in a beggar-like street cry, some were secretly teasing each other, and some were fast asleep...

Against the window was a long, old-fashioned account table, and a large armchair that could seat two people. Sitting on the chair was an old tutor wearing a melon-skin gauze hat and old-fashioned glasses, shaking his head and using a vermilion brush to correct the students' test papers, humming "zhī hū zhě yě" like a mosquito!

Suddenly, he slammed the ruler hard and shouted loudly, "Fusheng, come here!" Immediately, a student aged eleven or twelve, with a trembling and fearful expression, ran to his desk. The old tutor immediately twitched his beard and launched into a long series of praises. At the same time, the mahogany ruler repeatedly struck the palm of the student's hand!

Only then did he catch sight of me, the uninvited guest standing at the door. He stood up to greet me, cleared his throat with a "hmm-ha" sound, and spat out a mouthful of thick phlegm; it seemed like he was clearing his throat first, and then preparing to talk to me!

He told me that he was a top-ranked juren in the Qing Dynasty and had been teaching for over twenty years. In the past, the students' tuition fees were enough to support his family, but in recent years, schools have sprung up, snatching their livelihood, and the authorities also want to strictly ban them. He sighed greatly, and his sobs did not stop!

His stubborn, impoverished, and bitter expression not only failed to arouse my sympathy but instead made me feel completely disgusted. I have always maintained that in the current era of vigorous reading and literacy, such private schools, which are internally corrupt and harm other people's children, must be banned and eliminated!

Starting from Proverbs 150

— A Certain Person

Now, writers often pride themselves on being erudite, and the so-called classics they quote in their articles were mostly proverbs at the time. Moreover, more than half of the three hundred poems selected and preserved by Confucius are clearly folk songs. These kinds of ancient sayings and ancient poems, regardless of which aspect they describe and praise, feel particularly beautiful and make people reluctant to let go, even today. The value of so-called ancient sayings and ancient poems lies in this.

This is because these proverbs mostly come from nature and contain no artificial embellishments. However, when they are passed down orally, they disappear in a flash, making it difficult to feel much interest. Once they are included in the writings of writers, they become like bright pearls and beautiful jade, impressive and remarkable, and become excellent materials for writing.

Each region has its own unique proverbs, and the creation of these proverbs is based on life and society. Therefore, one can see the form of life and social phenomena in proverbs. For example, the groans of the sick, the cheers of those enjoying themselves, the laments of the frustrated, the sorrows of the wounded, and the anger of the enraged are all unavoidable. Shanghai's social life is relatively complicated, and at present, it is even more full of various abnormal states. Therefore, Shanghai's proverbs are chaotic and complicated, unlike the simple and superficial ones in other places. So, if you want to study the actual situation of Shanghai's social life, starting from these proverbs is the best way. At the same time, these proverbs are also of relatively greater value in literature.

Mr. Wang Zhongxian's recent book, "Illustrated Shanghai Proverbs," has now been published. Mr. Wang has not only lived in Shanghai for a long time but has also deeply entered various societies. In particular, Mr. Wang is also a playwright, so he has a deep understanding of Shanghai. Therefore, he is especially good at writing this book. In addition to including all the Shanghai proverbs, the book also states their origins in a clear and concise style and connects them to stories. After reading it, one feels that Shanghai's viscera are all in this book. At the same time, to increase interest, Mr. Xu Xiaoxia has also drawn pictures for each chapter to show its form and sound. Therefore, the book is beautiful and difficult to match. In terms of its contribution in various fields, its value is even immeasurable. (The entire book is forty hundred thousand words and costs one yuan and two jiao. It is published by the Social Daily Newspaper Office on Ningbo Road, Guangxi Road.)

Only Men Give Way to Women on the Tram 151

— Qingquan

The Imperial Fragrance Drifting Record 152

— Originally Written by Princess Qingdeling, Translated by Qin Shouou

Chapter 30: Facing the Sun with Lotus Flowers in the Morning

On the day the Empress Dowager decided how to punish the corrupt Guangdong Governor, although she had disregarded sentimentality, abandoned benevolence, and resolutely announced her views, these views were only driven by a temporary sense of justice and did not come from her original intention. Afterwards, she thought of the merits of the punished person's ancestors and father in this dynasty, as well as several achievements he had shown in the past, which made her feel infinitely uneasy. The smile on her face completely disappeared, and her face was always iron-blue, as if she were holding a belly full of sorrow and anger. Seeing this, I couldn't help but feel strange. Although I also knew it was because of the rebellious minister, at that time, I didn't know the nature of this punishment was so serious and the impact was so lasting. So, I was very strange as to why she was so uneasy after the punishment.

Because of the Empress Dowager's unhappiness, the entire inner palace was once again plunged into a gray atmosphere as usual; all the eunuchs, palace maids, and even female officials were worried, fearing that they would be caught and used as tools for venting her anger. Everyone didn't even dare to walk casually, tiptoeing and trying their best not to make any noise. They reduced their speech especially, and even if they had something to say, they only used whispers. In fact, the Empress Dowager didn't have any anger, she just felt very sad in her heart, as if something was stuck in her throat. Seeing her open her lips repeatedly, wanting to say something to me, but repeatedly held back, it can be seen that she was really thinking very painfully in her heart. (380)

Character Sketches

Anecdotes of Pan Xiao Jiu 153

— Nan Ding

Mr. Pan Xiaojiu of Wumen had long been an official and, tired of his travels, returned to Shanghai, where he enjoyed a reputation for chivalry. He was most skilled in the art of character divination, unlike Xie Shi of the Southern Song Dynasty, and was considered a top-tier master of the art. He had no pre-written scrolls, and would interpret characters chosen at random, offering explanations that were extremely logical and reasonable. Therefore, friends and relatives often sought his guidance on difficult matters, and his instructions invariably proved miraculously effective. As a result, he was known as the second Xie Shi.

Pan and Zhang Zongchang were very close in their early years and had a deep friendship. After Zhang became the military governor of Shandong, Pan did not go to him despite several invitations, because of Zhang's poor reputation in governance. Later, when Zhang came to Shanghai and met Pan, he dragged him to Jinan. Pan had no desire to become an official, so in Jinan, he indulged in pleasure with Cheng Guorui, Qiu Fengzhen, and others, and did not often meet with Zhang. At this time, Li Jinglin had just retreated from Zhili to Jinan. Tianjin had been taken by Feng Yuxiang, and Li wanted to use Zhang's military power to recover Tianjin, but because Feng's power was at its peak, he had not yet launched an attack. One night, Li had a dream in which he saw three large spirit tablets, with the words "Kui Wu" on the top of the central one, "Fan Chong" on the right, and "Fan Yu" on the left. After waking up, the vision was vivid in his mind, and he was greatly surprised. He told Zhang about it, but Zhang was a crude man and knew nothing about character interpretation. At this time, Qiu Fengzhen was serving as the president of the Shandong High Court and was by Zhang's side. He thought of Pan's character divination and told Zhang and Li about it. Zhang and Li had also heard of Pan's miraculous accuracy in character divination, so they immediately ordered Qiu to invite Pan to the governor's office to study the dream. The next day, when Pan arrived at Qiu's invitation, Li immediately asked Pan to interpret the six characters from his dream. After looking at them, Pan, noting that it was currently mid-December, gave a very insightful explanation. He said that the first character "樊" (Fan) contained two "木" (wood) characters and a "爻爻" (gua) character in the middle. The two "木" characters combined formed the character "林" (Lin), as in Li Jinglin. It was winter, and the trees were withering. Meeting the "六爻爻" (six-gua) meant that there would be war. Splitting the "林" (Lin) meant that Li Jinglin had lost Tianjin, but the "樊" (Fan) character was on the left, so it would have to come from the right. Winter would pass and spring would arrive. In spring, the trees would flourish. Under both "樊" (Fan) characters were "大" (big) characters, forming "兩大" (two big), meaning that they could each gain a big advantage with Zhang, recover Tianjin, and once again accomplish a great feat. Furthermore, the character "崇" (Chong) meant "宗" (ancestor) under a "山" (mountain), representing relying on Zhang Zongchang like Mount Tai. The character "鈺" (Yu) meant gold and jade, representing the brotherhood of Wu Ziyu. By relying on these two, they could regain the lost territory. The character "魁" (Kui) came from "鬼" (ghost) plus "酉" (you), meaning ugly enemies who were not worth worrying about. "斗" (dou) plus "門" (men) rightly indicated a time of battle. The character "武" (Wu) meant stopping the spear, but this was a time for using force, so how could they stop the spear? Moreover, the spear in this case was not a correctly written spear, but a reversed spear, so they had to guard against someone turning against them. After the interpretation, Li was amazed by the mention of Wu Ziyu, who was indeed a sworn brother. Zhang wanted to know whom Pan was referring to with the talk of turning against them. Pan initially did not say, but as he was leaving, he secretly told Qiu that the person who would turn against them was Fang Zhenwu. This was hinted at to Zhang, as the character for defending against treachery, "防" (fang) contained the character "方" (fang), and the phrase "正當用武" (at the time of using force) contained the characters "正武" (Zhenwu). Sure enough, within three days, Fang Zhenwu turned against them. The following spring, Li Jinglin, with the help of Zhang and Wu Ziyu, regained Tianjin. Pan's character divination had been completely validated.

On another occasion, a friend asked Pan to divine the character "腦" (brain). Pan immediately warned him to be careful, because the character "腦" (brain) had the "災" (disaster) character at the top and the "凶" (ominous) character at the bottom. Although the disaster had not yet occurred, there would be an ominous event. The friend then asked who would be in danger and what the ominous event would be. Pan said that the character "腦" (brain) could be written as "脳", containing the character "凶" (ominous), meaning that someone would die. The part of the character next to the "肉" (meat) looked like "月" (moon), resembling flesh and blood but not quite flesh and blood, meaning a daughter-in-law. He should quickly be on guard. The friend asked when the death would occur. Pan added the "月" (moon) character to the character "期" (qi), which contained "月" (moon), indicating this month. Moreover, the parts of the character, properly arranged, formed the numbers "二十六" (twenty-six) and "八" (eight) and "三" (three) - meaning the 26th at 8 PM. Later, the friend's daughter-in-law died on the 26th of that month at 8 PM. This kind of miraculous accuracy was no different from Xie Shi's. Furthermore, when Li Jicai attacked Jinan at Baliwa, Zhang Zongchang asked Pan to divine the character "一" (one). Pan determined that there was no cause for concern, because that year was the year of the Ox (丑), and adding "一" (one) under "牛" (ox) formed the character "生" (life). However, in the year of the Rabbit (卯), adding "一" (one) under "卯" (rabbit) would form the character "死" (death). Later, Li Jicai was indeed defeated and retreated, and Zhang died in the year of the Rabbit.

Mr. Pan, at the request of friends, has now decided to set up his divination table in Shanghai starting on August 1st. From now on, if we have any difficult matters, we can ask Pan for guidance, so as not to go astray.

Little Western Heaven 154

— Written by Zhang Henshui

Chapter 17: Do Not Ask About a Daughter's Gender and Difficulties, Everyone Competes to See a Noble Person's Face and Admire Their Lofty Character

Zhiqian said: It seems that Mr. Zhang has already agreed to help you, right? Huanhua held the empty cup, staring blankly, her brow slightly furrowed, as if she was in great distress. Zhiqian said: It's not surprising. People who are guests elsewhere just want to earn some money to take home and enjoy, why would they help others? Huanhua said in a very low voice: That's for sure. It's just... it's just... he shouldn't have lied to me. She struggled to utter the word "I," and immediately two streams of tears rolled down her face. She didn't have time to use a handkerchief to wipe her tears, and just wiped her eyes with her fingers. When Zhiqian saw her crying and heard her say she had been deceived, he didn't need to ask what happened next. So he said: I think this Mr. Zhang is very busy today, maybe he doesn't have time to help you. Huanhua said: Mr. Cheng, didn't you hear? He just said that he could only help me tomorrow. He knows I'm eager to return home, so he said that on purpose. Even if I really waited until tomorrow, he might not be able to help me. Zhiqian said: Do you think that's him deceiving you? Huanhua said again with tears: Mr. Cheng is a smart person, do I need to explain it in detail? What else does a drifting woman have that people can deceive? It's just that... the night before last, he was drunk and very happy. He promised me ten dollars for expenses on the train. He also said that he had a relative who was an official in Nanjing and would introduce me to him. He could send me a train ticket to Shanghai and even send me some money. Naturally, I believed him. Yesterday, everyone was together again, busy with Miss Zhu's affairs. I sat in his room until after one o'clock in the morning. He said that guests were coming this morning and told me to go back, so I had to go back. (280)

Education News

Ministry of Education Strictly Orders Colleges Not to Accept Students from Unregistered Private Schools 164

According to a key official in the Ministry of Education, students and graduates of unregistered private schools should not receive the same treatment as students from registered schools. This is clearly stipulated in the regulations for private schools. Unregistered schools have no legal basis, and students who rashly enroll in them will not be able to obtain graduation qualifications approved by the Ministry of Education upon completion of their studies. Rights conferred by law, such as subsidies for students and eligibility for various examinations for graduates, cannot be enjoyed equally with students from legal schools. This matter is related to the students' own interests, and the choice of school should be carefully considered. The Ministry of Education has issued earnest announcements to students, hoping that they will all understand this. Recently, the Ministry of Education again issued a notice to public and registered private colleges, stating that from the 24th academic year, they must absolutely not accept transfer students from unregistered colleges or students from unregistered high schools. From now on, students should pay even more attention when applying to schools. The original order is recorded below:

It has been found that public and registered private colleges should not communicate back and forth, wasting procedures and being improper. We hereby reiterate the previous order: from the 24th academic year, schools must absolutely not accept transfer students from unregistered colleges or students from unregistered high schools. If any have already been admitted, they should be removed immediately and should not be mixed in and reported to the Ministry. Rejection is of utmost importance. In addition to sending to the branches, it is ordered to comply. This order.

Ministry of Education Instruction

Improvements to University Systems in Shanxi and Anhui Provinces 165

Shanxi University: The Ministry of Education issued an order to Shanxi Provincial Shanxi University on the 2nd, stating, "The Ministry has dispatched personnel to inspect the school and has received a report. After detailed review, there are many aspects that need to be improved. The main points are outlined as follows: 1. The School of Education was formed by merging the former Shanxi Provincial School of Education. The Ministry previously ordered the integration of all departments of the school into the School of Liberal Arts. The name 'School of Education' should be immediately abolished. Existing Chinese Literature students should enroll in the School of Liberal Arts. The Department of Education should temporarily suspend enrollment. The Department of Electrical Engineering in the School of Engineering lacks equipment and duplicates the electrical engineering program at the Provincial Vocational School of Engineering. It should be discontinued starting next year. The mining and metallurgy departments should be merged into a mining and metallurgy department, with specialization in the third year. 2. Many departments in the school have established positions such as deputy director, and some departments have also established deputy directors, which is inconsistent with university organizational regulations. These positions should be immediately abolished. The number of staff members is excessive and should be reduced to save expenses. Of the 90 faculty members, 58 are part-time. Their expertise does not always align with their duties, and their research achievements are minimal. In the future, the number of part-time faculty members should be reduced, and excellent and qualified full-time professors should be hired to guide research and improve teaching efficiency. 3. The allocation of funds in the school is unreasonable. Equipment expenses account for only 6%, leading to a significant lack of equipment. Office expenses account for 19%, exceeding the Ministry's standard by a large margin. The allocation should be revised, with equipment expenses no less than 15%. Office expenses and salaries should be strictly reduced to supplement equipment. 4. The equipment in the school's laboratories and factories, as well as instruments and specimens, are outdated and rudimentary. Most books, except for ancient texts, are outdated and do not meet the needs. Western books and magazines are scarce. The above three points should be implemented, and any remaining funds should be used to improve equipment. 5. The curriculum design of the school is inadequate and should be revised and implemented effectively. The departments of the School of Engineering should add physics and physics experiment courses, reduce mathematics hours, and complete them in the first and second years. Factory practice should begin in the first year. Surveying practice for the civil engineering and mining departments should be scheduled during the second-year summer vacation, with a duration of at least three weeks, and should be supervised by professors. 6. The teaching materials in the school are outdated lecture notes, and the content is not practical enough. The teaching methods are misguided, and there are few experiments. The course progress is not well-planned. The grades on various test papers are poor. The school should strengthen the training of newly admitted students to improve their level. 7. Moral education in the school is lax and lacks positive measures. Although the students are simple, many are spiritually decadent. In the future, faculty and staff should pay close attention to moral education, striving to cultivate a spirit of simplicity and hard work. The order requires compliance and sincere improvements to be reported."

Anhui University:

The Ministry of Education also issued an order to Anhui Provincial Anhui University on the 2nd, stating, "The Ministry has previously issued key points to urge improvements. Based on the report of the inspectors, the school has generally paid attention to the implementation over the past year. However, the following points still need to be implemented and reported for review: 1. The School of Agriculture is approved to establish one class of agronomy this year. Enrollment should be strictly limited to 20 students. Training in basic subjects such as physics, chemistry, and biology should be emphasized, and equipment should be improved. 2. The school's physics and chemistry equipment, such as wireless electricity, gas and electricity communication, modern physics, and physics instrument repair room, are rudimentary. The gas plant and combustion chamber are missing. Psychological instruments are insufficient. There are very few complete sets of scientific journals. The above equipment should be added to facilitate teaching and practice. Sanitation and sports venues should also be established as soon as possible. 3. There are still too many part-time faculty members in the school, and many are unqualified. In the future, recruitment must be strictly controlled, and the number of part-time faculty members should be reduced. The full-time system should be implemented. The number of staff members should also be reduced. 4. Although the recruitment of new students and the restriction of leave and absence are slightly better than before, they still need to be strictly implemented to improve the level and quality. This order."

National Mandarin Education Association

Telegram from Suzhou Urging Attention to Symbols

Promoting Local Dialects Aligns with Ministry Orders, Welcoming Children from Jiangsu and Shanghai to Participate

The Fangyin Committee of the National Mandarin Education Promotion Association is promoting Suzhou phonetic symbols, starting on August 1st of this year, which is National Children's Year. It is also seeking 1,000 young Suzhou dialect speakers to assist in the promotion. The details are as follows:

Promoting Local Dialects Aligns with Ministry Orders

The Fangyin Committee of the association promotes Suzhou phonetic symbols based on the Ministry of Education's order in May 1920, promoting phonetic symbols: "Thousands of symbols can annotate national sounds, or annotate local sounds. Teachers and students should all learn and practice them, making it easy to promote supplementary education for the public." And in July of the same year, the Ministry of Education ordered 25 measures for provinces, cities, and counties to promote phonetic symbols: "4. Provincial, city, and county departments should investigate local dialects. 5. Compile small booklets for learning local dialects with phonetic symbols, and pay attention to local homophones with symbols, explaining them in the local dialect to facilitate promotion." In 1922, the Ministry of Education ordered the National Language Unification Preparatory Committee to compile local phonetic symbols according to the important dialect regions of the country. The Suzhou phonetic symbols promoted this time are the latest revised version of the National Language Association. All activities are completely based on laws and regulations and are not in violation.

Welcoming Participation, Offering Textbooks

The first step in the association's promotion of Suzhou phonetic symbols is to use wireless transmission to teach, seeking 1,000 young Suzhou dialect speakers to assist in the promotion. Children aged 10 to 15 in Jiangsu and Shanghai are welcome to participate. Those willing to participate can obtain registration forms and methods from the Suzhou Park Library and the Shanghai He De Road Fo Yin Radio Station. Fill out the registration form and send it to the association at No. 3 Ping Le Li, Xizang Road, Shanghai. The association will immediately send a young Suzhou dialect speaker certificate and a Suzhou phonetic symbol textbook. At the end of one month, the association will reward young speakers with excellent results. The first prize is a scholarship of 30 yuan, the second prize is 10 yuan, the third prize is 5 yuan, the fourth to tenth prizes are 3 yuan each, the eleventh to twentieth prizes are 1 yuan each, and the twenty-first to one hundredth prizes are a piece of learning supplies each.

Broadcasting Programs Change Daily

The association will broadcast the Suzhou phonetic symbol textbook taught at the Shanghai Fo Yin Radio Station (980) from 2:15 PM to 3:00 PM daily, starting on August 1st. There will be one lesson per day, and classes will be held as usual on Sundays. Stories, novels, plays, riddles, folk songs, common sense, and popular tunes will also be broadcast, as well as prize-winning tests to help listeners' interest. All programs except textbook teaching will change daily. Please check the broadcasting news in various newspapers. The association and Shanghai Yamei Company jointly organize a radio Mandarin course, which is broadcasted non-stop every day from 5:20 PM (on Shanghai Broadcasting Station (1100). The textbook is attached to the company's China Wireless Radio Half-Day Publication. Listeners can learn by listening to the book.

Mayor Wu Welcomed them at a Tea Party Yesterday

Representatives from various countries in the International Junior Summer Camp and representatives from southern China have gathered in the city. They are scheduled to take a boat to Qingdao today. Mayor Wu Tiecheng specially held a tea party at the Gaoqiao Seaside Bathing Beach yesterday to welcome them. The Youth Association also held a grand banquet in the evening to entertain them. The National Association of Chinese Youth Associations has specially added a tour itinerary to allow the representatives to visit scenic spots in China. The details are as follows:

Mayor's Welcome

Mayor Wu Tiecheng of the city specially held a tea party yesterday to welcome the representatives of the International Junior Summer Camp from various countries and China. The location was originally set at the City Hall Auditorium, but later, in order to allow the representatives to visit the Gaoqiao Seaside Bathing Beach, at 2:30 PM yesterday, all the representatives took a special boat prepared by the municipal government to Gaoqiao and transferred to cars to the Seaside Bathing Beach. Mayor Wu's representative, Zhang Tingrong, warmly entertained them, offering Chinese and Western refreshments, and inviting all the representatives to swim. At 5:00 PM, they took the original boat back to Shanghai. At 6:30 PM in the evening, the Shanghai YMCA specially held a grand banquet to entertain the representatives. All the directors of the Youth Association and General Secretary Lu Ganchen attended. At about 7:00 PM, the guests and hosts dispersed happily.

Departure to Qingdao Today

In addition to the representatives from Japan, Korea, and northern China, the representatives from the Philippines, Honolulu, and various places in southern China, including more than 60 people from Ningbo, Fuzhou, Guangzhou, Hong Kong, Nanjing, Yunnan, Hangzhou, and Xiamen, are scheduled to take the Xinjiang ship to Qingdao today and transfer to Yan'er Island to enter the camp. Zheng Hanjun, the executive secretary of the camp, and six Chinese leaders, including Tian Xingen, are also taking the same boat to Qingdao.

Tour Itinerary

The National Association of Chinese YMCA has specially added a tour to allow the representatives to visit famous scenic spots in China. The itinerary is as follows: (1) Beijing (Forbidden City, Temple of Heaven); (2) Great Wall for one day; (3) Two days on the way south from Beijing; (4) Jinan (Mount Tai) for two days; (5) Qufu for one day; (6) Two days on the way south from Qufu; (7) Nanjing for one day; (8) Hangzhou for two days. The entire tour will last for 14 days.

Overview of the International Junior Summer Camp: Zhou Shang The types of summer camps are divided into youth, junior, children, and girl scout camps. The origin of summer camps comes from the outdoor camp life of European naval and army student groups and boy teams. When the Boy Scouts emerged, the training of tents became a temporary fashion.

In 1918, the United Kingdom promulgated Article 17 of the Education Ordinance, which clearly stipulated that local educational administrative organs should do their best to create or assist in running summer camps. Denmark, Sweden, and Germany have the most remarkable achievements. Summer camps in the United States are also springing up like mushrooms. Last year, there were 575 along the Pacific coast. Japan, a neighboring country, is also learning and imitating, with the potential to surpass others. In recent years, our country has also volunteered to do it. Everyone already knows about the children's health camps in Tianjin, Nanjing, and Shanghai.

The summer camps run by various countries have already made headway. Therefore, the Junior Department of the World YMCA Association in Geneva initiated the organization of the "Pacific International Junior Summer Camp." The first session was held in Japan in 1929, with more than 100 representatives from 13 countries. The second International Junior Summer Camp was held in Honolulu in 1931. At this time, our country began to send representatives to participate. 1933 was the third session, and the location was in the Philippines. This year is the fourth session. It was decided the year before last to set it up in our country. The current camp address is assumed to be Qingdao Yan'er Island. This island is surrounded by the sea on all sides, with beautiful scenery, willow branches like curtains, and ripples like 　. Swimming and boating are very convenient. The Shanghai Youth Association has already sent staff to prepare.

The purpose of this camp is to connect the young people of the Pacific countries, to discuss the situation of the countries and life issues with a friendly attitude, so to exchange knowledge, skills, and customs, to seek understanding between races, and to develop the personality and鍛鍊 body of young people at the same time are equally regarded as important goals. The value of this kind of camp can be said to be that one day, it can correct physical and psychological defects, secondly, develop good habits, thirdly, enlighten the mind and morality, fourthly, produce a spirit of mutual assistance and cooperation, fifthly, approach the natural world, and sixthly, use leisure time to benefit the cultivation of temperament. In short, morality, health, and world harmony are the ideal goals of this camp and also the highest value of this camp.

Because this camp is hosted by the YMCA, the representatives from all places are also within the scope of the YMCA. It is estimated that about 122 people will participate this time, including 24 leaders from various countries. The participating countries include Japan, Korea, the United States, Hawaii, Canada, Siam, the Philippines, and other Pacific countries, as well as overseas Chinese living in the Far East. Our country has assigned 27 people from major cities such as Nanjing, Xiamen, Ningbo, Shanghai, Guangzhou, Changsha, Yantai, Fuzhou, Hangzhou, Hankou, Hong Kong, Kaifeng, Beiping, Tianjin, Jinan, and Qingdao, and invited 6 leaders. The qualifications of the representatives are limited to high school first and second-year students aged 16 to 19 and who are active.

The cost for each representative is about 54 yuan, including eight days of food, round-trip travel expenses from Shanghai to Qingdao, and registration fees, etc., but personal expenses are excluded. After the camp closes, a tour group will be organized for a two-week itinerary with voluntary participation. Places such as Beiping, Jinan, Qufu, Nanjing, and Hangzhou are all included in the program, and each person will need about 100 yuan. As for the daily routine of the camp, see the news in the education column of the August 2 newspapers, "Mayor Wu Welcomes the Representatives of the International Junior Summer Camp," so I will not waste words.

Municipal Party Department Guiding and Assisting in the Implementation of Children's Year 168

The Central Government has Issued Guidelines for Guidance and Assistance. The Department Appoints Member Cai Hongtian to Attend

The Central Government has designated this year, from August 1st to July 31st of next year, as the National Children's Year. The Executive Yuan and the National Children's Year Implementation Committee have successively sent letters requesting the formulation of guidance methods to facilitate guidance and assistance from local party departments. The Central Propaganda Committee has specially formulated an outline for the party department to guide and assist local Children's Year implementation methods and distributed it to various municipal party departments for compliance. The municipal party department of this city has already received this guidance outline. The department has appointed Executive Committee member Cai Hongtian to attend to guide and assist the association in its progress. The original letter from the Central Propaganda Committee and the guidance outline are as follows:

Letter from the Central Propaganda Committee: "Approved by the Executive Yuan, 'Designated this year from August 1st to July 31st of next year as Children's Year, and formulated the National Children's Year Implementation Methods Outline, please approve the guidance and assistance for the reason, and approve the letter from the National Children's Year Implementation Committee, please formulate the party department to assist the local Children's Year Implementation Committee to implement various official methods outline,' have successively arrived at the meeting. We have now formulated a party department to guide and assist the local Children's Year implementation methods outline of six items, in addition to replying to the National Children's Year Implementation Committee to order the various levels of the Children's Year Implementation Committee to comply and separately send letters, specially send the outline for reference. This is to you,' (omitted below)

Guidance Outline: "The party department guides and assists the local Children's Year implementation methods outline 1. (1) Each local Children's Year Implementation Committee should invite one instructor appointed by the local party department to participate in the guidance. (2) When each local Children's Year Implementation Committee holds a meeting, the instructor appointed by the party department should be invited to participate in the meeting, and the instructor may put forward various guiding opinions for public discussion and implementation. (3) Matters that the local Children's Year Implementation Committee consults for assistance in handling should be assisted as much as possible. (4) The local party department and its appointed instructor should make every effort to guide and assist the propaganda work and assembly matters of the local Children's Year Implementation Committee. (5) If the local party department believes that the matters handled by the local Children's Year Implementation Committee violate party principles or have major errors, it may present reasons to the local Children's Year Implementation Committee and request it to correct them automatically. If the committee does not accept it, the party department may submit a detailed description of the facts and request the superior party department to forward it to the superior Children's Year Implementation Committee for verification and processing.

Little Men (3) Original by American Ms. Alcott Translated by Zheng Xiaocang (Zonghai) 169

Ned was so engrossed in watching this exciting contest that he lost himself, and unknowingly he had gradually left his corner and ventured out. Later, a very active boy slid down the escalator, but because he used too much force, he couldn't control himself and fell off the escalator, slamming to the ground. Ned heard the sound and forgot himself, so he rushed to the person's side, thinking that he must have a broken head and be half dead. Who knew that the child's head had been constantly collided for eleven years, and it was as hard as a cannonball! So he just quickly blinked his eyes once, and after a while, he looked up at this new face quietly, and greeted him with surprise, shouting "Hello!" (Note 1)

(Note 1) Hallo is a greeting word to people, similar to the "hey" in our country. However, the Hallo here also implies a happy encounter, which seems to be difficult for the word "hey" to express completely, so it is translated directly.

"Hello," Ned also replied, because he didn't know if there was anything else to say, thinking that that kind of reply was the simplest and most convenient.

The youth on the ground didn't move at all, but asked, "Are you a new boy?"

"I don't know yet."

"What's your name?"

"Ned White."

"My name is Pang Tao Mo; would you like to go up and try it?" Tao Mo jumped up as if he suddenly remembered the responsibility of being a guest.

"I'm afraid I still won't do it, let's see if I can stay here," Ned replied, but his desire to stay grew deeper and deeper.

"Hey, Xiao Qiao, here comes another one. Come and say hello to him;" said the energetic Tao Mo, and then returned to his original game, with the same interest as before.

The boy sitting on the stairs heard him call and raised a pair of big yellow eyes, looked up and stopped the child with a thin and kind face. There was a kind of attractive power in his appearance.

Rumors Amplify Buyer Momentum; Bid Reaches $900

Huge Increase of $16.60

Following the rebound from the earlier reversal, the gold market continued to thrive yesterday. Although momentarily dampened by the loose exchange market, persistent buying interest and supporting rumors led to another surge. London spot gold increased by one and a half pence, and exchange rates slightly appreciated. Overnight unofficial trading had already pushed prices higher, reinforcing market confidence. Off-exchange pre-market trading opened at $92.30, then retreated to $91.00, before rising again to $93.40. The morning opening was high, with the central bank's official rates announced as flat for both the UK and US, and the customs gold unit also unchanged. Chinese Merchants Turn from Selling to Buying

Foreign Exchange Loosens and Then Surprisingly Tightens

According

To foreign dispatches, both near and far positions in London large bars were flat, the New York silver market was unchanged, Montreal forward silver prices increased by one point and remained unchanged, London spot gold rose by one and a half pence, GBP rose 125 against USD, GBP rose 3 pounds against FRF, USD rose 125 against GBP, FRF fell 25 against USD. The foreign exchange market opened in the morning with the near-term selling price of GBP at 1 shilling, 6 pence and 125, and USD at $37.4375, tightening by 125 and 3125 compared to the previous close. The central bank's official rates were announced as flat for both GBP and USD, and customs gold was unchanged. Market sentiment was slightly weak after the opening, and a loosening trend emerged. Shanghai selling hardened, but HSBC took advantage of the cheap prices and managed to maintain the market. Thereafter, Shanghai Bank repeatedly sold, HSBC announced flat GBP and USD rates, and foreign banks generally had buying interest, resulting in an extremely stable situation. Although banks had buying interest after entering the market, market sentiment was common, and Chinese merchants slightly supplied, resulting in a balance of supply and demand, and the process established a special change. Expectations for unchanged Indian silver further presented a peaceful trend, and banks also took the opportunity to sell high. The aftermarket saw banks immediately buying, with a tightening potential. As expected, rumors of restrictions on paper currency redemption at the Bank of China in Qingdao and elsewhere arose, and Chinese merchants suddenly bought, and speculator Luo also made up positions. Shen Bao Wireless Weekly

Talking About Single-Button Carbon Granule Microphones 178

— Shi Huaxin

In wireless broadcasting machines, carbon granule microphones are generally used. In more sophisticated broadcasting machines, condenser microphones and moving coil microphones are also used. Carbon granule microphones can be divided into two types: single-button and double-button. Single-button carbon granule microphones are mostly used in wired telephones, while double-button carbon granule microphones and other styles are mostly used in broadcasting machines. However, the biggest advantage of single-button carbon granule microphones is that they output the most with the same intensity of sound wave input, thus avoiding multi-stage amplification devices. The degree of distortion can be reduced to a minimum with proper adjustment. Due to the above advantages, single-button carbon granule microphones are most commonly used in amateur circles.

Its structure is shown in the first diagram. A is an elastic diaphragm, fixed to the microphone cover E with rubber bands FF. B'B are two carbon plates, with B' being fixed and B connected to the diaphragm A, vibrating along with it. C is extremely fine carbon granules between plates B and B'. G is a mica sheet, H is an insulated cover, and D is a circle of insulating paper on the four walls of the box. B and B' plates are also the connecting posts of the microphone. When we connect a DC power source to B and B' plates, current flows from plate B through the carbon granules to plate B', or from plate B' through the carbon granules to plate B. At the same time, when we speak into the microphone, the diaphragm A vibrates with the sound waves. This vibration is transmitted to plate B. Because plate B' is fixed, the carbon granules between the two plates are subjected to different pressures. According to the characteristics of the carbon granules, the resistance between plates B and B' either increases or decreases accordingly, and the current flowing through either increases or decreases accordingly. It is inversely proportional to the resistance and directly proportional to the pressure (the resistance of carbon granules is inversely proportional to the pressure). Because the pressure is directly proportional to the sound wave, the waveform of the current change is exactly the same as the sound wave, achieving the purpose of using the microphone.

The current that can pass through the microphone is very small. If the current exceeds a certain limit, sparks will occur between the carbon granules, rendering it useless. The maximum current that ordinary single-button microphones can pass is approximately one-tenth of an ampere. When there are no sound waves acting, the resistance is approximately 50 to 100 ohms, and the maximum power consumption is o.ixo.ixoo, equaling one watt. In addition, there is a low-impedance single-button carbon granule microphone with a resistance of approximately 10 to 20 ohms. The maximum current limit is half an ampere, and the maximum power consumption is five watts.

The maximum amplitude of diaphragm A in ordinary microphones is approximately four-thousandths of a millimeter, 0.0025mm. If the amplitude is too large, the waveform of the output current cannot be the same as the sound wave. For example, if the sound wave received by the microphone is a sine wave, when the amplitude of the diaphragm does not exceed four-thousandths of a millimeter, the output current is also a sine waveform. If the amplitude gradually increases beyond the limit, the waveform of the output current will not be a pure sine wave, but a combination of sine waves and their odd and even harmonics, resulting in distortion. The degree of distortion increases or decreases according to the amount the diaphragm amplitude exceeds the limit.

In application, the combination of a single-button carbon granule microphone and the amplification stage uses an amplitude modulation transformer (see the second diagram). The mixed resistance of its primary stage is approximately 100 or 200 ohms. The microphone power supply can use a six-volt DC power supply, and a 100 or 200 ohm potentiometer can be connected across the power supply to adjust to the most suitable voltage. The secondary stage of the microphone transformer is connected to a 100,000 ohm potentiometer to manage the output voltage.

Wireless Electricity Cures Cancer 179

— Pao

The uses of wireless electricity are endless. In addition to communication, there are various unexpected applications. With various wireless electricity therapeutic devices, our lives have an extra layer of protection. Even "cancer," which has always been considered difficult to cure, has recently been treated with definite and rapid methods using mysterious wireless electricity waves.

George Lakhovsky has devoted the most effort to the issue of treating cancer with wireless electricity waves. Lakhovsky initially used electromagnetic waves with a wavelength of two meters to treat plants suffering from white tumors caused by a type of tumor-causing microorganism. In the first few days of the trial, the disease seemed to grow and spread, but dozens of days later, the tumor suddenly disappeared and gradually healed. Lakhovsky thus discovered that cancer could be treated with electromagnetic waves and delved into further research.

Later, Lakhovsky created a type of ultra-shortwave oscillator that could simultaneously emit various different wavelengths, and the experimental results were even better. At this time, more and more people became interested in this issue, and continued research sprung up like mushrooms. One time, an experiment was conducted on 300 cancer patients, and the results were extremely good. Two cases, previously considered hopeless, were completely cured.

Six years ago, Lakhovsky designed another type of amplitude-modulated wave transmitter that could simultaneously emit various wavelengths from 400 meters to 10 centimeters. Due to the effects of harmonics, interference, and heterodyne, waves with wavelengths close to infrared radiation and even equal to the wavelengths of light visible to the human eye were actually present simultaneously. The experimental results of this machine were extremely good. Even terminal illnesses that could not be treated with X-rays and radium pills could be cured with ease. Lakhovsky also claimed that this type of cancer treatment device did not cause artificial fever during application.

Lakhovsky’s New Electrical Therapy Machine 180

Economical Small AC Two-Tube Radio 181

— Zhi

—Improvement of AC/DC Radio—

I recently assembled a two-tube radio. The vacuum tubes used were a 6C6 and a 12A7 each. The former handles the work of a single-stage feedback detection, and the latter's task is low-frequency amplification and rectification. The experimental results show that, apart from the average selectivity, other aspects such as sensitivity and sound quality are quite satisfactory.

The circuit diagram of this machine is shown in the figure, and the numerical values and capacities of each component are detailed in the diagram. This machine has a wide range of radio wavelengths, from 10 meters to 500 meters, all of which can be listened to without missing anything. A total of six 1.25-inch radius four-pin plug-in coils are used. The design of the bands and coils is omitted due to limited space.

This machine can be used with 110 volt or 220 volt AC power sources. The B voltage is directly taken from the commercial AC power source and then obtained by rectification and filtering. The filament voltage is taken from the transformer after voltage reduction.

Although two vacuum tubes with different filament voltages are used in the machine, only one filament secondary coil of the power transformer is used. This is nothing more than a slight consideration, and it is not difficult to understand the reason. It is said that mass-produced radios mostly use this method to supply various vacuum tubes in the machine. Its economic convenience can be imagined.

Although this machine can only be used with AC power, its economic use of electricity is truly unmatched by AC/DC machines (the power consumption of this machine is less than about 10 watts, while if the machine is used as an AC/DC type, it must consume at least 50 watts or more).

If you want to make the power transformer yourself, you can stack 1.52 pounds of silicon steel sheets to 26 mm. The primary coil should be wound with 2,400 turns of No. 36 enameled wire, and a tap should be taken at the halfway point for use with a 110 volt power source. The secondary coil should be wound with 128 turns of No. 24 enameled wire, and a tap should be taken at 64 turns for the 6C6 filament. For the winding procedure and matters that should be paid attention to, please refer to Mr. Xuelun's masterpiece in Issue 122 of this magazine.

Steps for Assembling a Radio for Beginners (Conclusion) 182

— Xuelun

(4) Adding a High-Frequency Amplification Stage

The function of high-frequency amplification is to amplify the weak high-frequency signal received by the vacuum tube and then input it to the detection stage, so that the detection tube can obtain a considerable voltage, so the efficiency is very high, and high-frequency transformers are usually adjustable, so selectivity and sensitivity can be increased. In areas where there are many radio stations, or if you want to receive broadcasts from distant places, it is advisable to add a high-frequency amplification stage.

Now, you must first remove the original spider web board and replace it with a cylindrical coil. Take two Bakelite tubes with a diameter of 32 mm and a length of 76 mm. The coil winding method is as follows:

High-Frequency Transformer Take a Bakelite tube and wind 105 turns of No. 30 enameled wire for L1. At a distance of 3 mm, wind 24 turns of the same wire for L. The starting end of L1 is connected to the grid of the high-frequency amplification tube, and the ending end is grounded. The starting end of L is grounded, and the ending end is connected to the antenna. The two coils are in the same direction.

Detection Coil Take another Bakelite tube and wind 105 turns of No. 30 enameled wire for L3. Then, with No. 36 enameled wire, wind 45 turns for L4 at a distance of 3 mm from the ending end of L3. Then, take a 20 mm wide insulating paper and wrap a layer on L3. Wind 50 turns of No. 36 enameled wire for L2. The starting end of L2 is connected to the plate of the high-frequency amplification tube, and the ending end is connected to the B positive. The starting end of L3 is connected to the grid capacitor, and the ending end is grounded. The starting end of L4 is connected to the high-frequency coil, and the ending end is connected to the plate of the detection tube. The direction of the three coils is the same.

When assembling a radio, everyone knows that the most difficult thing to assemble is the high-frequency amplification stage, but the high-frequency amplification stage does not have profound theories or require clever technology. It is just that high-frequency amplification is prone to induction, and the amount of induction between the secondary coil of the high-frequency transformer and the secondary coil of the detection must be absolutely the same. Therefore, in addition to using aluminum isolation shields for the two coils, aluminum shields must also be used to isolate the No. 39 and No. 36 vacuum tubes to prevent mutual power effects.

After the new high-frequency amplification stage is connected, the entire radio is completed. The circuit is shown in Figure 6. At this time, it is best to carefully check for any errors, then connect the power source, turn on the power switch, and slowly rotate the dial and potentiometer. When the speaker emits a whistle, turn the potentiometer knob back a little until the oscillation stops properly. At this time, a very clear sound can be emitted from the speaker. If the volume is too low, or the sound is unclear, or it makes strange noises, you can adjust the compensation capacitor of the dual-gang variable capacitor. If it is still not clear, it is because the secondary coils differ too much and must be rewound. The components used are as follows:

L, L1 High-Frequency Transformer winding method see this article

L2, L3, L4 Detection Coil winding method see this article

R 500 ohm fixed resistor

R1 75,000 ohm fixed resistor

C 5 trillionth farad fixed capacitor

C1 Trillionth farad fixed capacitor

V No. 39 or No. 44 vacuum tube

The article Steps for Assembling a Radio for Beginners has been serialized three times, occupying a lot of valuable space in this magazine. The author deeply apologizes. In the second continuation of this article, the power transformer section, the secondary high voltage was found to be wrong. It was mistakenly copied from the manuscript for use with vacuum tubes such as 6D6 and 6F1. It should be changed to a secondary high voltage of 400 volts, wound with 1,680 turns of American standard No. 32 wire, and a center tap should be drawn.

Simple Two-Tube Shortwave Radio 183

— Yong Yan

The receiving range of a shortwave radio is far beyond that of a broadcast radio. An ordinary two-tube radio with a single-stage regenerative detection and a single-stage audio frequency amplification is considered to have achieved excellent results if it can receive broadcasts from 1,000 to 2,000 miles away. If a shortwave radio with the same conditions is used, it is not difficult to receive shortwave broadcasts from Europe, or even telecommunications from the United States on the opposite side of the earth, can be easily received from a small two-tube shortwave radio. This article introduces how to make a simple two-tube shortwave radio as a preliminary tool for us to develop shortwave treasures.

Please see the attached diagram for the circuit diagram of this radio. The numerical values of the components are marked in the diagram. A total of four plug-in coils are used? Miscellaneous Notes 184

— Chen Xianwen

(1) Thoughts on Photoelectric Tubes:

Photoelectric tubes are considered a fashionable and useful item in the modern scientific community. Many precise instruments or machines use them. Ordinary people always think that their eyes are reliable, but when compared to this electric eye (another name for photoelectric tubes), they are far behind. Sensitive photoelectric tubes can easily detect the light emitted by a candle 3 kilometers away. Because it has such sensitivity, it is often used for precise detection work, such as sound movies, stellar photometry, picture transmission, television, and automatic light signals.

(2) Properties of Sound:

The sound we usually hear has a certain limit to its vibration frequency (the average person hears between 20 and 10,000 times per second), but its intensity, if less than or greater than a certain value, cannot be distinguished or causes a painful sensation. The minimum sound that can be heard (meaning that sounds smaller than this point cannot be heard) has an intensity called the Threshold of Audibility. If the intensity of the sound slowly increases until it reaches the point of causing pain, this intensity is called the Threshold of Feeling. The intensity of sound required for the Threshold of Audibility and the Threshold of Feeling varies with the frequency of the sound. Their relationship is briefly summarized below:

Sound Frequency Threshold of Audibility Threshold of Feeling

(3) Thoughts on Vacuum Tubes:

The filament current of the vacuum tube in the radio should be kept to a minimum within the possible range, but without reducing the effectiveness. This is because it can prolong the life of the vacuum tube. The Operating Voltage of an ordinary vacuum filament is 90% of its Rated Voltage, and the effectiveness is not reduced. This little knowledge should be noted by economical amateurs.

Publishing World

What I Hope from the Commercial Press 185

— Zhang Sumin

The Commercial Press is the largest publisher in China, and everyone knows this. The morality and knowledge of its general manager, Mr. Wang Yunwu, his managerial talent, the efforts of his internal staff, and the excellence of its organization are also admired by everyone. Since January 28th, the Commercial Press has worked even harder, and the number of new books published has been increasing day by day, which is a good phenomenon in our cultural world.

However, it is precisely because we respect and love the Commercial Press that we have even greater hopes and stricter criticisms of it. Based on this motivation, I would like to share some of my personal hopes for it.

The low level of the publishing industry in China today is a reflection of the low level of knowledge and education in our society. There are few good books that are compiled and written, and even fewer good translated books. Most translated books are just black words piled on white paper, making them impossible to read. Because of my usual faith in the Commercial Press, I naturally "look at" the books it publishes with different eyes. To be fair, its books are generally better. However, when I read them carefully one by one, I also feel that there are few good ones and many bad ones. Even translated books are full of errors. The reason for this can be traced back to two points:——

1. Being too polite and sentimental to "celebrities" while simultaneously paying too much attention to temporary profits. The works of celebrities should be good. However, some celebrities in China are created by "bragging." Although the bragging is big, the knowledge and writing are still shallow. For example, a recent famous work by a certain celebrity published by the Commercial Press, if viewed from the perspective of a foreign university professor looking at a undergraduate student's graduation thesis, is simply "failing," or at least should be "rewritten." First, because the title of the book does not match the content. Second, because the translations used in the book are inconsistent. Third, because there are too many contradictions and errors in the book's content. However, the Commercial Press published the book without changing a word! The book costs three or four dollars, and buying it is regretful. From the "content" point of view, it is just a waste of a few dollars. However, "laymen" will regard it as a "masterpiece" and take it as an "authority." The harm of this "erroneous doctrine" far outweighs the loss of a few dollars. This cannot but be said to be that the editorial department of the Commercial Press is too sentimental to "celebrities." I hope that the Commercial Press will strictly review the content of manuscripts in the future, regardless of the author's name.

However, surprisingly, such a book that cannot pass the test, and at a selling price of more than three or four dollars in China today with its devastated economy, has surprisingly become a bestseller with a third reprint. From a profit-seeking point of view, the Commercial Press has a high vision, and I have a low vision; that book is beneficial to the Commercial Press. However, this kind of sales is temporary and cannot last. Because most people who buy books, like me, buy one to learn from the celebrity's boasting. However, after reading it, they realize that they have been greatly deceived and dare not recommend others to buy it again. Therefore, even for the sake of profit, the editors of the Commercial Press should advise the author to slightly modify the title and content and then publish it again, so that sales may be sustainable. Why value temporary profits?

2. Emphasizing quantity over quality and not being strict in selecting manuscripts. The Commercial Press releases new books every day. In terms of quantity, it is not small in China's current situation. However, books are different from ordinary commodities and cannot be "mass-produced." People who buy books want to take the books to study in order to gain knowledge and learning. If they open it and immediately find that the content is superficial, or even the reasoning is unclear, making them confused; or even the format is incomplete, such as the source of materials, reference books, etc., not mentioning a word. If it is a translated version, there are several sentences on one page that are incomprehensible, or even entire paragraphs that are incomprehensible, then what is the use of such books? The books of the Commercial Press are relatively good, but there are still many books of this kind. I hope that the editors of the Commercial Press will be stricter in selecting manuscripts in the future. The so-called strictness does not necessarily mean rejecting manuscripts; that is, for acceptable manuscripts, detailed annotations should be made on the places that should be deleted and revised, so that the author or translator can make their own deletions and revisions before publishing them. This is also a method of strictness. If it is a specialized book, it is best to have experts in the editorial department review it, or occasionally invite outside experts to review it, which is also possible.

The above two hopes can be applied to the general publishing industry. However, I am specifically saying this to the Commercial Press because, with the Commercial Press's qualifications and abilities, it is easier to implement and can take the lead in promoting it in order to improve the quality of publications.

Japan's Ordinary Publishing Law 186

— Zheng Zongkai

The types of laws applicable to publishing in Japan can be divided into ordinary publishing and newspaper publishing. Ordinary publishing is publishing that is subject to the "Publishing Law" and is further divided into so-called ordinary publishing and subscription publishing. Subscription publishing is publishing that is subject to the "Subscription Publishing Law" in addition to the "Publishing Law." Newspaper publishing is publishing that is subject to the "Newspaper Law."

So-called ordinary publishing refers to publishing that is subject to the "Publishing Law" but not subject to the provisions of the "Subscription Publishing Law" and the "Newspaper Law." Not only are standalone books, paintings, maps, photographs, etc., considered ordinary publishing, but also publications such as magazines that record academics, skills, statistics, and advertisements.

1. Persons Responsible for Ordinary Publishing

In Japan, authors, publishers, and printers are all responsible for publishing to a certain extent. These people are called "persons responsible for publishing." Let's explain them separately below:

(1) Authors According to the Japanese "Publishing Law," an author refers to writing, compiling documents, and creating drawings. For notes of speeches or lectures, the speaker or lecturer is the author. However, if the reporter, speaker, or lecturer permits self-publication, the notetaker is considered the author. The compiler of a book is the author; the translator is the author; the school, company, association, etc., that publishes, is the representative who submits the report to the authorities with their signature.

(2) Publisher According to the Japanese "Publishing Law," a publisher refers to someone who is responsible for selling and distributing. The publisher is not limited to the author and their heirs, but must be someone who is in the business of selling documents and drawings.

(3) Printer According to the Japanese "Publishing Law," a printer refers to someone who is responsible for printing. However, it does not refer to someone who is responsible for individual printing activities, but someone who is responsible for all printing activities. Therefore, someone who owns a printing shop is considered a printer, and if a printing shop is jointly owned by several people, the person who represents the printing shop in business is considered the printer.

2. Publishing Reports

The Japanese "Publishing Law" stipulates that when publishing documents and drawings, the author must submit two copies of the published work to the Ministry of Internal Affairs within three days from the date of publication, excluding the number of days it takes to arrive. When a government office publishes, it must send two copies of the published work to the Ministry of Internal Affairs before publication. The reporting form must be jointly submitted by the author or their heirs and the publisher, but for non-sale items, only the author and the publisher need to submit the report. If the publication is not protected by copyright, or if the author or their heirs are unknown, only the publisher needs to submit the report. For publications from schools, companies, associations, etc., the report must be jointly submitted by the representative and the publisher.

If additional volumes are added and published sequentially, it is necessary to report each time. However, for magazines, etc., if permission is obtained from the Minister of Internal Affairs, the reporting procedure can be omitted, and only the published work needs to be submitted. When reprinting, no report is necessary except in cases where corrections, additions, subtractions, and the addition of annotations, appendices, and drawings are made. For special publications such as letters, communications, reports, association rules, leaflets, and photographs, it is not necessary to complete the reporting procedures at all. (To be continued)

From Writing to Publishing (3) 187

— Importance

How is the paper mold made? It involves giving the typeset and proofread letterpress to the mold-making workers, who then use paste to glue multiple layers of paper together. They place this paper onto the letterpress and tap it with a large brush. Don't think just anyone can do this job. If you are an amateur, and you hit it a few times, breaking the paper, you have to replace it. If you are not careful when tapping, the paper will shift, and the strokes of the characters will become doubled; if you tap unevenly, some areas will be clear while others are unclear. The book cast from this plate will be blurry and unreadable, and no one will buy it.

After the paper mold is made, it must be placed on a stove to be pressed and dried. If it is not pressed well, or if the heat is insufficient, the paper mold will be useless. If the heat is too high, the paper mold might burn, and the lead type of the letterpress will also be destroyed, so extreme care is required during drying.

Nowadays, large newspaper offices use machines to make paper molds. This is not only done well, but it also takes less time. For example, making a paper mold manually takes one hour, while a machine takes less than two minutes. They use a special, thick foreign paper for making these molds. Just place the letterpress on the machine and press it, and it's done. It is evident that machine industry is much better than manual labor.

Casting the Plate

After the paper mold is made, it is sent to the plate-casting workers. They use a machine to hold the paper mold in place and pour molten lead into it. When opened, it becomes a lead plate identical to the letterpress. This lead plate is much more convenient to use on the printing press than the letterpress. However, casting lead plates also requires skilled workers to do well. If the lead is too hot or not hot enough, or if the paper mold is damp, the cast will have flaws and cannot be used for printing. Skilled workers can cast a usable plate almost every time, rarely needing to recast one. Unskilled workers often cast several plates in a row, none of which are suitable. An ordinary paper mold can be cast more than ten times. A not-so-good paper mold becomes useless after being cast six or seven times.

If zinc plates are used in the middle of the typeset when the lead plate is cast, the zinc plate areas must be repaired by the workers because the character feet of the zinc plates are shallow. If not repaired, the surrounding areas will get ink during printing. Repairing lead plates is not easy either; if you're not careful, you can damage the characters. Skilled workers will not damage them, and even if they do, they can plate some lead onto it and repair it to be the same as before.

If a paper mold has been made, you can correct any uncorrected typos on the paper mold. If a lead plate has already been cast and then you discover a typo, the workers can dig and correct it for you on the lead plate; however, if the book has been printed, there is no way to dig and correct it on the book.

Printing

Once the lead plate is cast, it can be placed on the printing press to print the book. However, the book is a small booklet, and the paper is a large sheet, so one large sheet of paper must be printed with several pages of the book. The size of the book is not fixed; there are octavo, duodecimo, sextodecimo, 20-mo, 23-mo, 24-mo, 25-mo, 32-mo, 36-mo, 40-mo, 46-mo, 50-mo, 60-mo, 64-mo, and even 128-mo sizes. The arrangement of the lead plate is different for each size. If one plate is arranged incorrectly, the page order will be reversed during binding, so it not only requires care, but it is simply not an easy job. If you arrange one plate incorrectly and discover the error later, the resulting compensation you have to pay will be enormous!

Also, attention must be paid to aesthetics. If one plate is arranged too high or too low, or is crooked, losing the unity of the whole book, the book will lose its aesthetic appeal. Moreover, even if it is unified, if the head and tail margins are too high or too low, or if the plate's position is too far in or out, it will also lose its aesthetic appeal. Furthermore, it might cause the characters to be bound or cut off during binding, which is not only unaesthetic but simply turns it into a pile of waste paper. So, it may seem that the machine is printing the book and the workers are merely moving the paper, which is very easy, but once you see all this, you will know that everyone's job is not easy.

Let me tell you some more about the issues when printing books, which are paper and ink. Paper can be glossy or matte, thick or thin. Glossy paper is easy to print on, while matte paper is not; paper with moderate thickness is easy to print on, while paper that is too thick or too thin is not. Furthermore, there are many names and types of paper, and each type of paper has different paper properties, such as being hard, loose, smooth, or brittle. Because of these different properties, they absorb ink differently, so one must understand the properties of the paper and what kind of ink to use, which will reduce difficulties during printing.

After the book is printed, it is sent to the binding workshop (i.e., bookbinding factory) to be bound into a book.

Binding

Binding is the final procedure in making a book. After the book is printed on the machine, it is sent to the binding workshop, where they first cut the large sheets of paper into small sheets, and then send them to the workers to fold them page by page. Most of these book-folding workers are women. After folding, the binding workers take them and, according to the page order, place them on the table, arranging them into book blocks, and then bind them.

There are several binding methods, such as "thread binding," where thread is used to sew through the fold of each section; "perfect binding," where three holes are punched near the spine and sewn with thread; and "wire stitching," where wire is used instead of thread. The first two are done manually, while the last one is done by machine. This refers to small-scale binding workshops. In large binding workshops, all types of binding are generally done by machine instead of manual labor. However, "wire stitching" is used for binding magazines and other thin publications because it is faster. As for thick books, it is generally not used because the wire rusts easily and can damage the book.

The binding styles include Western binding with cloth covers, Japanese binding with flat spines, French binding with uncut edges, and fine Chinese binding. After the book block is bound, the cover is then applied. Speaking of the cover, it is also quite troublesome. Hardcover books require gold stamping, and paperback books require color printing. The book cover design also takes a lot of effort from the designer, as an unaesthetic design will significantly reduce the reader's desire to purchase the book. After it is bound, it is then packaged and sent out for sale.

Conclusion

The window display during book sales and the design of advertisements also require a lot of effort from people, but we won't talk about that for now. Just looking at the procedures from writing to publishing a book, one already feels the amount of trouble and effort it takes. The above is the common knowledge of publishing. I hope the readers won't think it's too brief and not worth reading! (The End)
